After I completed for you, oh sons, this book, which is the last of the science of medicine with its complement, and I reached the end in it, from its explanations and declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this treatise which is a part of the operation, that is, surgery by hand.
Since the operation by hand has been neglected in our region and time, and has been completely abandoned; until perhaps its science has perished and its track has been cut off; and there have not remained of it except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which hands have altered; and error and hesitation occurred to them, until its intentions were closed and its use was prolonged: It seemed to me that I should revive it with the organization of this Treatise in it, according to the method of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation; and that I should come with the forms of iron instruments of cauterization, and other instruments of work; with the addition of declarations, and with the preparation of what is necessary.
The reason for which a good practitioner of it with his hand is not found in our time, is: that the art of medicine is long, and its author must exercise beforehand in the science of anatomy, which Galen described, until he knows the functions of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and tendons, and their number, and their outgoing, and the veins' pulses, and quietness, and the places of their exits.
And because of that, Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We have already spoken of that at the beginning of this book.
Since he who is not knowledgeable about what we have said concerning anatomy, will not be cautious, and will already fall into error, by which men are harmed: as I have seen many of them, who boast about this science, and speak of it without knowledge, and without experience.
What happened was that I saw a physician make an incision into a scrofulous aposteme on a woman's neck and he cut some arteries in the neck, from which the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead at his hands.
And I saw another physician who presumed he would extract a stone from a man which had grown inside him over time, and the stone was large. He therefore approached him, and extracted it with a piece of the bladder. For the man died on the third day.
And I had already been called to extract it, and I saw from the size of the stone and the weakness of the man that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was receiving a stipend from a certain Duke of our land because of medicine: and it happened to a black eunuch who was with him that he got a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the physician acted with his ignorance, and pressed the fracture above the wound with poultices, and applied a tight bandage, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he treated him according to his desires. Afterwards he left him for some days and ordered him not to undo the bandage: and it stayed like that until his leg became apostematic and his foot, and it came to destruction.
I was therefore called to him: and I hastened to undo the bandage: and calmness followed, and he was freed from his pains.
But indeed the corruption had already been established in the limb: and I could not restrain it.
Then the corruption ceased to spread through the limb until it died.
And I saw another physician who perforated a cancerous aposteme, and it became an ulcer after some days, until the evil of it became great with its owner.
What is, that when it is pure cancer from melancholic humor, then it is not suitable to be pierced with iron at all, unless it is in a member that can tolerate it, so that all of it can be cut away.
And on account of that, O sons, it is necessary for you to know that the operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, an operation to which health is associated, and an operation in which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already excited in every place of this book, in which comes the operation, in which there is terror and fear.
For it is necessary for you to beware of that, and dismiss it: so that the stupid ones do not find a way to speak and to disown.
Receive therefore the measure with solicitude and protection, and your infirm ones with facility and firmness, and use the better way leading by the grace of God to salvation and praiseworthy succession: and dismiss dreadful anxieties of difficult healing: and lift your souls from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation enters into your faith and your commodity.
For it is more remaining to your glory, and sublime in this world, and afterwards to your quantities.
For Galen has already said in certain of his warnings. Do not call the evil sickness medicine: nor name the bad physician.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
The first Chapter.
Of the cauterization with fire, and sharp medicine cauterization, chapter and ordained from head to feet, and forms of instruments, and ironments of cauterization: and all that which is necessary in the operation.
The second Chapter.
Of cutting and piercing, bloodletting and puncture, and wounds: and the removal of arrows, and similar things to that: and the entire chapter, ordered in the forms of instruments.
The third chapter.
Of restoration and dislocation, and the cure of twisting, and similar things to that: a chapter, ordered from head to foot, and in the forms of instruments.
But before which thing it is necessary to recall the quality of its cauterizations and brandings: and in what complexions they are exhibited.
I say therefore, that the discourse on the quality of cauterization and branding is a profound and subtle science, and a hidden secret.
And many wise men have spoken on it, and disagreed about it: and for myself it is enough to take a little from their discourses, fearing a prolonged discussion.
I say therefore, that cauterization is suitable for every complexion, which is with material and without material: excepting two complexions, which are a hot complexion without material, and a dry complexion without material.
But in the hot and dry complexions with material they disagree. For some have said that cauterization is suitable for it. And others have said the opposite, namely that cauterization is not suitable for a disease which is from heat and dryness: since the nature of fire is heat: and it is unsuitable to cure a hot and dry disease with something hot and dry.
And he said, the one who says the opposite of that: that which is treated by cauterization becomes a remedy in every hot and dry ailment that occurs in the bodies of men: for when you compare the body of a man and its humidities to the complexion of fire, you find the body of a man cold.
And I indeed say through his speech: that the experiment has already revealed that to me many times.
But it is not fitting that one should come upon that, unless he has already been proven and exercised in the chapter of Cauterization's final exercise, and knows the diversity of the complexions of men, and the disposition of ailments in themselves, and their causes, and accidents, and the space of time of them.
From the remaining complexions, however, there is not above the use fear: and especially in cold and humid ailments. For all physicians have already agreed upon them, and do not disagree with the remedy of Cauterization in them.
And know, my sons, that from the secret of cure by Cauterization with fire, and its goodness over Cauterization with burning medicine is: for fire is simple, whose action does not penetrate except to the member which is cauterized: and does not harm another member joined to it, except with a little injury.
The action of burning medicine penetrates to that which extends from the members: and perhaps makes occur in a member an ailment of difficult healing, and perhaps kills.
Fire, however, on account of its subtlety and goodness of its substance, does not do that, unless it overflows.
Now that has become known to us through experiment, on account of the length of service and study with art, and position upon the truth of things: and because of that I will excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not, I would not be allowed to reveal to you in my book a secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies of expulsion, which expels diseases, demonstrated by philosophical speech, which will be keen in your minds.
And you should know, sons, that they themselves disagree on the time in which it is suitable to apply a cauterization, and they put the best time in the spring.
And I say that a cauterization is suitable at any time, because the harm that occurs on account of the time is outweighed by the benefit that is drawn with the cauterization. And especially if a cauterization is on account of pains from necessary pains, strong, urgent ones, which do not tolerate delay: because what is feared from them is that a greater evil will occur, which is worse than the small harm that occurs on account of the time.
And let it not fall into your minds, O sons, that which they do not consider, except the common and stupid physicians, namely that the diseases which are healed by a cauterization, do not always return: and they think that this is a consequence, and the thing is not as they think: because a cauterization is not, unless in place of medicine, which alters the complexion, and evacuates the humors which are the causes, for which pains occur.
However, a cauterization surpasses medicine by the swiftness of its health, and the virtue of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion: and it is possible that the disease may return at some hour of time according to the complexion of the weak person, and the location of his disease, and its virtue: and what is prepared in his body from the aggregation of superfluities in it: and what pervades into it in acquiring them from foods, and similar things from causes, unless a disease is made, in which a cauterization is administered.
A subtle inflammation in a member with little superfluity of blood and humidity, such as a cauterization of the tooth, because of pain, and similar to it, is possible that the pain does not return in it. But that happens in few.
And I speak to the common people again, that cauterization is the last of medicine, is a straight speech: not according to what they themselves intend in it: since they believe that there is no cure which agrees with medicine, nor with another thing after the application of the cauterization.
The thing is contrary to that, and the intention, that cauterization is the last of medicine, is not, except that when we administer modes of cure in some disease, and those medicines do not agree: then we administer in the end of the thing cauterization, and it agrees: therefore it falls, that cauterization is the last of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish medical men understand.
The ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron: and they did not say that except because of the equality of gold, and the sublimity of its substance: and they said that it does not produce pus in the place of the cauterization. But it is not true absolutely: since I have already proved that, and found that it does not do that in certain bodies without others.
And cauterization with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said. Truly however when you ignite the cauterization fire from gold, it is not declared to you, when it is ignited according to the quantity that you use, because of the rubedo of the gold: and when it approaches the cold, and if you add ignition on top of it, it melts in the fire, and turns into sheets.
Wherefore the artisan falls from that in work: and because of that cauterization with iron is made by us more swiftly and nearer to the truth for the operation.
And I have already arranged this chapter on cauterization, following the chapters, and I have arranged them from head to feet, so that they provide to the inquirer what he wants from it.
Head II or Chapter II, Head
This cauterization is beneficial for the domination of humidity and cold over the brain: which two are causes of heaviness, and an abundance of flux of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and an abundance of sleep, and pain in the teeth, and pain in the throat: and universally all sickness which occurs due to cold, such as palsy, and heaviness, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar to those diseases.
The method of cauterization is that you should precede the weak with a purging medicine to clean the head for three nights, or four, according to what the strength of the weak person requires, and their age, and their habit.
Then instruct them to shave their head with a razor. Then make them sit between your hands in a square shape, so that they have already placed their hands on their chest.
Then place the root of the palm of your hand on the root of their nose between their eyes. Wherever your middle finger touches, mark that place with an incision.
Then prepare the olive cautery for ignition, whose shape is this.
Then place it on the marked location with an incision, and lower it, by which your hand is contracted little by little, and you turn it. Then lift your hand quickly, and inspect the place.
If you see that it has already drawn out from the bone a quantity of head alkali, or a quantity of zeherb, then lift your hand. And if not, you will strike your hand with the iron itself or with another from it if it becomes chilled: until the bones which I mentioned to you are visible.
Then take something from salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cotton in it, and put it on the place: and leave it for three days.
Then put on it a cotton soaked in butter, and leave it on the place, until the eschar is destroyed by fire. Then treat it with the ointment Tetrapharmacon, until it is healed.
Now they have said, that the more a wound remains open, the more it emits pus: therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them have said, that the skin should be cauterized to the bone: and that the cauterization should be held, until there is a thickness like that of bone.
Then scrape away what has been burned from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that it is necessary to perforate with a cauterization iron to the extreme, until it makes an impression on the bone for a mold, so that the bone falls, which is made like a form of a comb: or the instrument that women use to insert a letter of the alphabet: and they extract, what vapors of the head expire from this place, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then treat it, until it becomes consolidated.
To me, however, these two kinds of cauterization do not seem suitable except in certain men according to the way of fear.
And to leave it, is better with me for the health of itself.
For the head is weakened from the solution of its natural continuity: as we have testified in the other members: and especially when the head is weak and feeble by nature: and a certain kind of cauterization is more salvatory and better with me, and I use it: therefore operate with it for health.
Chapter Three.
When there is chronic pain throughout the whole head: and it is prolonged in the sick person, and they are treated with henna, and cohchia, and head purges, and oils, and plasters. And especially if it has already been cauterized with a single cauterization, which we have described, and none of those things are of benefit to it: then consider. For if the head of the sick person is of strong natural constitution, and it is not weak, and it meets with vehement cold: then cauterize with another cauterization under that a little. Then cauterize it on the entire horn of its head with a cauterization, so that it does not penetrate too deeply through the skin, and a quantity is discovered from the bone, which we have described. And cauterize it with a single cauterization on the back of its head, in the place which is called the "uas": and it is a place where the ventose is applied: and elevate your target in this, and you will not discover bone. For the sick person meets with vehement and diverse pain from the pain of all the other cauterizations of the head.
And I will call this Cauterization in its proper place: and it is necessary that there be a cauterization, with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and its occiput more subtly than the cauterization with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter Four.
When there is pain and inflammation in one part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and it is treated with medicines that cleanse the head, and the rest of the treatment which I mentioned in the divisions of diseases is administered, and none of those things are of benefit: then cauterization in this case is according to two methods: either cauterization with medicated cauteries that burn: or with iron.
Cauterization with acute burning medicine is such that you take one tooth of a gear, and strip it, and cut off its extremities on both sides. Then cut the place of pain at the time with a broad scalpel, until a place under the skin is made, in which the dense part is captured.
Insert it therefore under the skin, until it is hidden: then bind above it with a bandage of decent constriction, and leave it for fifteen hours; then undo it, and extract the tooth, and leave the wound two days, or three: afterwards put on it a plaster submerged in butter, until the place makes pus: then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you want to make it with certain burning medicines, which I wrote about in the twelfth treatise, on Medicines for burning.
Cauterization of it with iron is according to this method. Fire cauterization, whose form is this.
And it is called a Clavulus: because the form of its head is like the form of a nail, in which there is something curved, and in the middle of it is a certain small prominence.
Then put it on the place, and hold your hand: and you withdraw the iron little by little with speed: and let the quantity that is burned be from the thickness of the skin, as its middle. And lift your hand, so that the artery which is below is not burned, and there occurs a flow of blood.
Then soak the plaster in salt water, and put it on the place, and leave it for three days: then put a plaster with butter: afterwards treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you want, cauterize this half of the skull with the edge of a second cauterizing knife. And beware of the incision of an artery in this half of the skull, not being old is a special property.
On the method of cauterizing in the old half of the skull.
When you treat the half of the skull, with what we have said from the preceding cure, and what we have said in the divisions of ailments, and the treatment is not effective: and you see from the ailment that what we have said about the first cauterization with medicine or with fire does not suffice for it, then it is necessary to make an igneous cauterization, until it becomes white after you apply a sign above the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or about that: and put your hand in place of one, and press it until you cut the artery, and penetrate up to the mouth.
Truly it is necessary for you to beware of the continuity of the jaw, which moves during mastication, lest the side or nerve which moves it be burned, whence spasms occur.
And let this be above caution and beware of the flow of blood from the artery that has been cut. For in the cutting of it there is fear, and especially for him who is ignorant of what he does, and is not careful, nor experienced: and he undertakes the operation with this from the beginning.
And I come with a reminder of the regulation of the flow of blood that occurs from an artery according to its own method, and in the place proper to this book.
What if you see from the ailment that this cauterization is not sufficient for it, and you see the body of the weak one enduring a cauterization in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cauterization that we have spoken of in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with a cauterizer having two knives. For cauterization is better than this and more beneficial.
On the method of cauterizing for earache.
When pain occurs in the ear from cold and it is treated with solutions and the rest of the treatment that we mentioned in the division, and the pain is not relieved, then cauterization by fire: and this is what is called a puncture, whose shape is this.
Then puncture it with that after its ignition all around the entire ear, as it is rotated: or around both, if pain is in both. And stretch yourself with the cautery from the root of the ear for a little while, after you have marked the places with ink, and let the quantity of the cautery be ten punctures on the entire ear, or about that.
Then treat the places until they heal.
On the method of cauterizing for Colic.
Chapter Seven.
Colic that is treated with cauterization is not except for the types which occur from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of illnesses.
And it requires cauterization of the type that occurs from dryness and spasm of a nerve.
When you treat this type of colic with hiera and purgings and gargling and your treatment does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize the weak area with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little below the temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And put your cauterization on the opposite side from the weak part. For softening does not occur except in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cauterium directly on the extremity of the ear above, under the horn of the head a little, and another on the temple: whose length is according to the length of the thumb. And put your hand with a cautery until the quantity of the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of a Cautery, and it is a type of knife, whose form has been described above: nevertheless it is not more refined than that little, as you see: and it should be a knife with a bit of excessive thickness.
Then treat the place, with what has preceded, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in old Apoplexy.
When the Apoplexy has become old, and you treat it with what we have said, and your medication is not effective, and the weak person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on every horn of his head, and a cauterization in the middle of the head, as we have said, and a cauterization on the back of the head, according to what has preceded: and the method of the cauterization should be according to what has preceded.
And also it is cauterized with a Cautery over the bone of the stomach: and this is the most extreme method.
Then let it be treated with what has preceded.
Chapter 9.
It is necessary that at first the weak person should be given a drink of great hysteria, and purging pills to cleanse the brain.
Then shave the entire head of the weak person, and put on its back an emplaster of snail as described in the treatment of emplasters: and apply it several times.
This indeed is the method of Cautery: and do that according to the same order which I mentioned there.
If therefore he is healed by it, it is good. If not: then make for him three cauteries on the back of his head, which should extend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye: and put between each cauterization the thickness of a finger.
Then treat the cauterization, together with what has preceded.
If however you use an application, and he is weak and unable to tolerate it: then apply a cauterization in the middle. What if you use an application: then cauterize it on top of the two horns.
Then treat it, until it is healed: and let the cauterization be according to the form that has been described beforehand.
On the method of cauterizing for paralysis, and softening.
Chapter 10.
It is necessary that you proceed with the cleansing of the head with care, and with what we have said.
Then shave the head of the weak person: afterwards cauterize it with a cauterization in the middle of the head, and with a cauterization on top of every horn of the head, and with a cauterization on its back, and with three on the vertebrae of the neck.
If however you are afflicted with a disease of softening of the body in many places, and he is weak and unable to tolerate it, and the disease is strong: then cauterize him with four cauterizations on the vertebrae of the back, and the last one with a cauterization, until much of its skin is burned, and lift your hand. Then treat it, until it is healed: and thus the cauterization of an olive.
On the method of cauterizing for epilepsy.
The epileptic is not cauterized, unless it is he whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
It is necessary therefore that you cleanse his brain first with care, and with the rest of the treatment which we have said in the division: when he is greatly weak, or is unable to tolerate the acceptance of medicines.
If however he is a boy, who does not tolerate medicines, then administer a gargle, and cleansing mastications for the brain, before that for many days with improvement of foods.
Then shave the head of it, afterwards cauterize it with one cauterization in the middle of the head, according to what has preceded in manner: and cauterize another on the occiput and over every horn of its head with a cauterization. What if it is weak and strong and has been tolerating, then cauterize it with the cauterizations that I mentioned in one having paralysis and a softening of the body over the spondiles of the neck and the spondiles of the back: and let the Cauterium be olive oil according to the method which has preceded.
If however it is a weak child, then put a subtle cauterization, according to this method.
On the method of cauterizing for Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humours and gross phlegm, then cauterize it with the Cauterizations that we mentioned in one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is a superfluity inclined to melancholy, and it is a body of an infirm person humidified, then give to it in a drink what will cleanse its brain, according to that which has preceded in the division: afterwards shave the head of the infirm person, and make then a little roll made from linen, as a circle.
Then put it in the middle of the head: and let the infirm person sitting squarely be held from every side.
Then present an ointment or plaster. And it is worthy made from old butter of ewe's milk. And warm it over a fire with a tempered measure of heating, which the finger can tolerate, when it is inserted into it. Then apply it on the middle of its head in a circle, and leave it until it cools down.
Do that to the infirm person every week once, with the rest of its good regimen, until it is cured.
Or if you use it, cauterize it by making many small points, in addition to which you should apply the cautery with a gentle hand while smelling it.
This type of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then put on it a cushion soaked in butter, or hen's fat.
On the method of cauterizing with water descending to the eye.
Chapter 13.
When the beginning of the water in the eye is declared to you by signs, which I mentioned in the division, then begin and drink the weak one, with that which cleanses its head.
And guard it from all moistures, and make it sit in a bath, in fasting for some days.
Then command it to shave its head, and cauterize it in the middle of its head. Then cauterize it above the two temples with two cauteries, if there is a simultaneous descent of water in both eyes; or on one side, if there is a descent of water in one eye: and cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in width of the temples: and cauterize to stop the flow of blood.
What if you see anything of it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and cutting them, and caution from the flow of blood.
And when it is cauterized on the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries which are produced to the utmost.
On the method of cauterizing old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and frequent: and they are above the veins, and arteries which are on the manifest exterior head, it is verified that this is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities: then cauterize with the same cautery that I mentioned in the descent of water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries on the neck under the two bones. And if you notice an increase, then cauterize it on every side with a cautious eye, above the eyebrow with a small cauterizer.
On the method of cauterizing in the nasal polyp.
When you treat it with what we said in the division and the treatment is not effective then prepare and give a drink of weak cohosh for three nights afterwards shave his head and cauterize it with a moderate cautery iron with an olive oil cautery. Then cauterize it with a cautery of the neck, with two cauteries, above the two eyebrows under the hair a little.
And guard against the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the cautery of the neck.
On the method of cauterizing for softening of the Eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye becomes softened from illness or moisture then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries on every side and they will be stretched for two times and let the length of every cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow and do not move your hand with the cautery unless according to the quantity that is burned the third of the eyelid.
On the method of cauterizing the eyelid when inverted eyelashes prick the eye.
The cautery for this is according to two methods: either a cautery with fire or a cautery with burning medicine.
For the cautery with fire, instruct the weak one beforehand that he release his eyelashes if he is of those who clean them until they stretch and become even. If however they prick it at its base: then bind its eyes with a thread, so that they do not move, until they heal.
When therefore the healing and equalizing occur, then put the head of the weak one in your bosom: afterwards apply a mark above the eyelid of its eyes with encaustic, a mark which is according to the figure of the myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then put a piece of cloth soaked in egg white on the eye: or in a mucilage of psyllium above the eye.
Then apply cautery with a branding iron, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the figure that you marked little by little on many places, until the surface of the skin is burned, which is like the shape of the myrtle leaf, appearing entirely as its own.
And the sign of the health of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted, and the hair lifted up at the puncture of the eye.
Lift your hand then: and leave it for three days.
Then put on it a piece of cloth with butter, until the scab is eradicated. Then treat it with ointment, until it heals.
If some of the hair returns after an hour, and the eyelid becomes soft: then apply cautery again on that place, as you did at first.
If however the hair is on the underside: then cauterize it, until it lifts up to its natural place: and equals out so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is that you instruct the weak one to let the hairs go, until they grow out and equalize. Make from a piece of cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap, and from unabsorbed lime one ounce or about that; then rub them together with good friction, and make it with haste, so that it does not get cold. Then spread from it over the cloth which you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and put it on the eyelid of one eye, or two. And put under the eye a piece of cloth imbued with egg white: and let the head of the sick person be in your lap.
And put your index finger on the medicine, and press it for a little while. And you move it as often as the sick person feels the biting of the medicine: for its biting penetrates like fire.
While therefore it perseveres that which it has found, the biting, then let go of the medicine, and move it with your finger. When therefore the biting subsides, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And consider then, if you see the eyelid lifted, as it is lifted with contraction from fire, or with incision, it is good: and if not, then apply again upon it of the medicine on the place, where the medicine does not impress, and does not denigrate, until your operation is equal, and the eye is contracted.
Then put over it a cloth with butter, until the burned skin is eradicated. Then treat it with the ointment called diaphenicum, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you during the operation, to guard with utmost care, lest something from the medicine falls into the eye.
What if the eyelid becomes soft after some days, and something from the hair pushes into the eye, then apply again the medicine on that place which becomes soft from the eyelid itself, as you did at first. Then treat it, until it heals.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And you should know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness. Therefore your consideration should be this: and the way of rectitude will not be hidden from him who has a zeal for this art.
On the method of cauterizing in a tear duct fistula.
When you treat a fistula, with what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatment is not effective: then, it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Order the weak person to place his head on your lap, and let your assistant hold his head between their hands in such a way that it is not moved or agitated with his head.
Then put a cotton swab under the conjunctiva of the eye, or in the mucus of the eyelid above his eye: then apply the cauterizing iron, whose shape is this.
Let it be hollow, in the shape of a quill pen from one end, with which the cauterization is made: and if you want it to penetrate up to the other end, and if you want it raised thus.
However this hollow one is better for your work.
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and extract the sanies from it, and clean it: and if it is not open, then open it, and extract its pus.
Then put on it the cauterizing iron, which is made very hot.
And hold your hand for a little while on the cauterizing iron near the eye, towards the nose, so that your hand is not burned, or the weak person is disturbed: and you put the cauterizing iron in the fat of the eye, and consume it.
If I cauterize at the beginning up to the mouth, it will be good. And if not: then repeat the cauterization once or twice, if you judge that necessary: and diminish it for three days.
Then put a plaster with butter, and treat it with an excoriating ointment, until it is healed.
What if forty days pass and it is not healed: then put on it a sharp corroding medicine, until the mouth is laid bare: and scrape it according to what is described in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some of the first ones have described. Direct it to the place of the fistula, and probe it: then put into the same fissure a thin rod, that is, a subtle little tube, whose form is this. And pour into it a quantity of lead melted from a drachm, and hold your hand with the cane in good retention, and do not move the weak one at all, so that the melted lead does not run or penetrate to its eye.
And it is necessary that you put on the weak eye a plaster under white of egg, or in water.
For lead burns the place of the fistula, and heals it with a wonderful healing.
What if the fistula is healed, with what we have said about cauterization, and cure, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the opening of the nose, and reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what comes to its proper place.
On the method of cauterizing in the fissures of the lips.
Fissures often occur in the lip, which are called Pili, and especially in the lips of children.
When you treat these fissures with what we have said in the division of diseases and the treatment does not work, then apply a small cautery to the knife, according to this method.
And let it be shaped according to the fineness of the knife.
Then put the ignited thing quickly into the fissures until the cautery penetrates to the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with a plaster, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in a fistula of the mouth.
When an apostema occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus and ruptures: afterwards it becomes chronic and the pus flows out and a fistula forms: then you treat it and if the treatment does not work, then it is necessary to apply a cautery according to the quantity that the fistula can hold. Then insert the ignited thing into the opening of the fistula and hold your hand, until the ignited iron penetrates to its depth and bottom: do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards with what we have said concerning treatment, until it is cured.
If therefore the sanies is cut off and healed, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to probe the place and remove the corrupted bone according to what is found in its head.
On the method of cauterizing the gums and softened teeth.
When the gum is softened because of humidity and the teeth are loose and you treat it with medicines and it does not work: then put the head of the weak one in your lap.
Then apply a cautery, of which the form will be shown after this, so that you put a tube over the tooth: and insert into it the ignited cautery quickly: and hold your hand for a little while, until the weak one feels the heat of the fire has already penetrated to the root of the tooth.
And lift up your hand; then repeat the cauterization several times, according to what you need.
Then let the weak bone fill itself with salt water, and hold it for one hour: and spit it out.
For a dense movement is strengthened, and the gum softened is tightened, and the corrupted humidity is dried.
On the method of cauterizing in toothache.
When the toothache is due to cold, or there is cold or worm in it, and treatment with medicines does not help: then cauterization in it is according to two methods: either cauterization with butter, or cauterization with fire.
The cauterization of it with butter is, that you take the butter of a cow, and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a metal vessel. Then take the scab, and apply it to the extremity of the aching tooth. Then submerge it in the boiling butter: and apply it quickly to the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools: then repeat it several times, until the power of the fire penetrates to the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge a thread, or a scab in cold butter, and apply it to the aching tooth: and put on top of it a heated iron, until the fire penetrates to the depth of the hollow of the tooth.
The cauterization of it with fire is, that you direct a bronze or iron tube. And let there be in its body something of thickness, so that the sharpness of the fire does not penetrate to the weak tooth.
Then cauterize with fire, of which the form appears: and apply it to that tooth: and hold your hand, until the cauterization cools.
Do that several times, for the pain will be relieved, either on that same day or on another day.
And it is fitting with the application of that cauterization, that the weak part of his mouth be filled with good butter, and that he hold it for one hour; then he spits it out.
And this is the form of the Cautery.
Cauterize with whatever extremity you use second to that which is possible: and this is the form of the Cannula.
On the method of cauterizing in the tracts.
When the Strophulae are from phlegm and from cold humidities, and they do not obey digestion through medicines, and you use digestion of them quickly: then a cauterization with fire is concave, whose form is this.
Having two open extremities, so that the smoke can go out at the cauterization from one extremity to the other: and put the ignited thing on the aposteme once, and a second time, if you apply it there, until it reaches the depth of the aposteme.
Which if the aposteme is small: then put the cauterization according to the quantity of the aposteme.
Then leave it for three days, and put on it a plaster under butter, until that which the fire burned is removed.
Then treat it with a dentifrice ointment, until the form of the cannula is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in the roughness called, and the constriction of breathing.
When the humidities overcome the canal of the lung, and especially when that is with a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the weak one be evacuated first with soluble medicines.
Then cauterize it in the nostril at the root of the throat in the pressed place: and beware, lest you penetrate with the cauterization to the throat, nor to the skin, except a little of it.
Then cauterize it with a cautery at the junction of the neck on the last vertebra, and let the cautery be a moderate one, according to the method which has preceded.
Then treat it with what has preceded, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in diseases of the Lung, and Cough.
When the cough and disease of the lung are from cold humidities, and the weak person has no fever, nor consumption, nor an old disease: then cauterize him with two cauteries above the armpit in depressed, mild, vacant places. And cauterize with another on the middle of the chest between the two breasts: and let the cautery be a tube-shaped one according to the form which has preceded.
And if you need to cauterize with a puncturing cautery, which is called a Point, whose form has preceded in the puncturing of ear pain: and let the points be from thirty points up to almost sixty.
Then treat it with what has preceded, until it is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches, according to this form. Wherefore it is alleviated with that cautery, when you make with it one of the three cauteries.
Chapter 27.
When the head of the arm is dislocated because of humidities, and it does not return to its place from its dislocation within the hour, until it becomes accustomed to returning, then it becomes dislocated by a slight movement, which happens as we have already testified, then you should reduce the dislocation first. Then let the weak person lie on his back, or on his healthy side. Then elevate the cut which is inside the Titillici upwards with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint becomes dislocated inwards.
Then have a cauterization iron with two prongs. Whose shape is this.
Then cauterize the cut until it penetrates to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization comes with four cauterizations.
And when a cauterization is made with an iron having three prongs, then the figure of the cauterization is made with six points: and these are according to the subtlety of the undertaking.
And this is the shape of the iron having three prongs.
And when one is added to it in this manner, then there are eight points of cauterization.
Then put on the cauterized area pounded roots with salt. Then make the weakened part adhere to quietness, so that it is not moved for a period of time, until it becomes strong.
And if the dislocation is upwards, and it rarely happens, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a cauterizing iron, or by making many points.
For the joint becomes firm, and humidity is removed: and the weak part is healed.
On the method of cauterizing the Stomach.
When many colds and humidities occur in the Stomach, so that they extract it from its composition, and multiply the phlegm to it, and assiduous methods of curation, and do not strengthen: then it is necessary for the weak person to lie on their back, and stretch out their legs, and hands. Then cauterize with three cauterizations, one cauterization under the shoulder blade in the quantity of one finger, with a clavicular cauterizer, and two cauterizations below from the two sides of one cauterizer, until the figure of the cauterizations comes triangle-shaped. And let it stretch between both so that they do not join together when they make pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be the quantity of two thirds of the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without addition and if you want to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form and let the cautery that makes this cautery be one according to the figure of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking him who trembles at this cautery and it is that you mark on the stomach a point according to the quantity that you want with the encaustic then cauterize it with the point cautery then treat it with the treatment which preceded until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing the cold liver.
When there is pain in the liver from cold and humidity, or from thick flatulence, until it goes out from its natural passage, and the weak person is treated with what we have said, and it does not profit him: then it is necessary that the weak person respine over his shoulder, and mark with encaustic three cauteries according to this figure, and the same quantity on the lower liver below the hypochondria, where the elbow of the man penetrates: and let the space that is between each cauterium be the thickness of a finger: and let the cauterium be straight along the length of the body: and do not press your hand much with the cauterium.
And let the quantity of what is burned be from the thickness of the skin, the quantity of half of it not added: and let the weak person stand on his feet.
If however he is not standing, then let him be lying, who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of a cautery.
And it is possible for you to cauterize these cauterizations with a knife cautery, when there is subtlety and prudence in the art.
And beware, that you do not proceed to the last in cauterization, and the thickness of the whole skin is burned, where the whole body is burned, and it perforates to the intestines: for the skin there is thin, therefore know that.
On the method of cauterizing the apostema of the liver.
When there occurs an eruption, and you want to know, if that apostema is in the flesh of the liver, or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, there enters a weak pain, and heaviness without sharpness: and if it is in the tunic of the liver, with pain there is vehement sharpness: and you see now, that it has wearied its physicians with its cure.
It is necessary therefore that the weak man breathes upon his neck. Then figure the place of the apostema with a searing plaster: then ignite a cautery which is similar to a razor. And this is its form. And cauterize with it one cautery, until the whole skin is burned, and it perforates to the siphac, until all the pus comes out: then cure it with the cure of eruptions, until it is healed.
And it is not necessary that this species of cautery be used, except by one whose study in the art of medicine is prolonged: and through whose hands these sicknesses run with experimentation many times: then indeed he dares to undertake an operation of this kind.
But truly to leave it, is better for me.
On the method of cauterizing in the Pleura.
The ancients said, a cauterization with the roots of aristolochia for a cold Pleurisy is done in this manner. And it is, that you take from the roots of the dry long aristolochia, one root which is longer than the others, and it should be the size of a finger. Then submerge it in oil: and set it on fire. Then cauterize with one cautery in that which is between the connection of the jaw with the neck, and with two small cauteries under the guidance a little sloping towards the part, which is under the beard.
And with two cauteries also in that which is between the fifth and sixth ribs sloping towards the back a little: and with one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries to the back: one in that which is between the two shoulder blades: and with two cauteries on the two sides of the chest, below the cautery which is between the two shoulder blades.
And it is not necessary that you press your hand with the cautery, but rather let it be on the obvious skin smelling.
And some of the ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery made from iron like a probe: and they ignite it, and insert it inside between the ribs, until it reaches with it to the same apostema, and the pus comes out: as we have said in the case of Epatis' apostema.
But in this perforation with the cautery there is a fear that either the weak person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, for which there is no cure.
Chapter XXXII. On the method of cauterizing the Spleen.
When you treat an illness of the spleen, with what we have said concerning curation in the division of illnesses, and your cure does not help, then a cautery on it is done in three ways, all of which are correct.
One of them is to make three or four cauterizations in a line along the length of the spleen according to the shape of the liver's cauterizations, whose figure has preceded.
And let there be between each cauterization an amount in thickness of a finger, or a little more.
And let the method of the cauterization be the one we mentioned for the liver cauterization equally.
And do not press your hand with the cauterization, and let him be weak leaning on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: to hold the cauterization iron with two fingers, which we mentioned in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder: and raise the skin that is opposite the spleen, where the weak left elbow penetrates: and let your elevation be what you use to raise the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauterizations fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert two fiery irons together, until with them you penetrate the skin from the other side: then withdraw the cauterization iron: thus four cauterizations are made.
And if you should cauterize with another cauterization iron having three fingers.
Then take care that the cauterization, after you have applied it, discharges pus for many days: for it is more beneficial than all the other things which have preceded in the cure.
On the method of cauterizing for Dropsy.
The cauterization does not fall in Dropsy, except for hardened ascites.
When you treat a case of Dropsy with the methods of cure that we mentioned in the division, and the cure is not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize him with four cauterizations around the navel, and one cauterization on the stomach, and another cauterization on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two cauterizations on the back between the vertebrae, and one opposite the breast, and another opposite the stomach: and let the depth of the cauterization be near to the thickness of the skin.
Then diminish the open cauterization so that it emits pus over a long time.
And it does not reject the weak from cure after cauterization with it, for which two intentions ought to be applied to it, and healing will hasten to it with the help of God.
The form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be a clamp, according to the shape that has preceded it: and that with which the back is cauterized should be an olive, according to the shape that has preceded its form.
On the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When they have become abscessed in a dropsical person, and are filled with citrine water: it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot in the nocturnal, which is between the ear and the ring finger: and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it: then raise your hand: and do not repeat it at all.
For the citrine water will flow out, and the cautery should be according to this shape.
Then make on each of the two legs two cauteries, and let the cautery be made with the extremity of a knife-like cautery: and let the cautery be made according to the length of the leg, one under the knee, and another below it, around the middle of the leg: and on all the thigh make two cauteries: and diminish the open cautery without cure for a long time: so that some water flows out from it: then cure it with the rest which we have said.
On the method of cauterizing for relief of the belly.
Chapter 35.
When there is a solution of the belly from cold and humidities, until it debilitates the retentive and digestive virtues, which are in the stomach and intestines: and it is cured with modes of cure, and not healed: and you see the weak tolerant of cauterization of overflowing virtue, then cauterize it with a large cautery on its stomach, according to what has preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle clamp-like cautery: and a large cautery above the hips, or two cauteries.
And if you see excessive moisture and the weak tolerance of that, then cauterize it with a cauterizer on the chest and with a cauterizer on all of it; and perhaps you will add two small cauterizations near the great stomach.
It is indeed a advancing treatment, whose benefit does not fail.
On the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter 36.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, or one, and they are from gross, cold, or corrupt humors, and they are treated with what we said in the division, and the treatment is not effective: then cauterize with three cauterizations on the lower vertebra of the back under the almeidati for a short time in a triangular shape, and cauterize under the navel almost two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face breaking out in pimples, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cauterizer, according to what has preceded: and cauterize on his liver, and another on his spleen, with a clavicular cauterizer: and apply an open cauterization for some time: then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter 37.
When you remove ulcers, then prepare a cauterizer that resembles a razor. Then insert the ignited cauterizer into the ulcer that has been removed: and with your hand, until the cauterizer reaches the opening of the vein, from which blood flows: do this once or twice.
If therefore there are many ulcers, then cauterize each one with a cauterizer according to what we have narrated. Then treat them with that which is beneficial to them from ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cauterization iron on the alkatim, it is more so in the ulceration.
Of the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter 38.
When the weak does not undergo surgical incision and operation that we have described in its proper place, and is frightened by it, perhaps it may be healed with a cauterization.
When therefore a fistula happens to someone, and it becomes chronic, pus runs out of it, and corrupted moistures. It is worthy therefore that which ought to be done, that you should probe it with a subtle sound. Then recognize the quantity of its depth with the sound.
Then apply a cautery iron, which is similar to a probe. Then insert the ignited thing itself into the same fistula and the quantity in which the clamp entered.
And repeat the cauterization over it, until all those corrupted bodies are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity of your necessity.
And beware of the burning of the nerve, if it is there, or of the large vein: or if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then beware of all these places.
And do not do that, unless when the fistula is in a fleshy place: and you think, that it is not penetrating.
Then take care of the place until it is healed.
If however the place is sealed, and matter is cut off from it, and it remains thus for a long time: then know that it is already completely healed.
And if matter is not cut off from it, then know that it is penetrating, or in its depth there is a corrupted opening, or something like that: whose mention will come in its proper place.
On the method of cauterizing the kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys from cold or from thick flatulence and it is weakened because of that, then it is necessary to cauterize it above the alumethene over the kidneys themselves, to cauterize each kidney with a cauterizing iron, whose description has preceded.
And perhaps we will cauterize it again on the same alumethene. Three lines appear where it has been applied. Therefore they will be more lasting in the healing.
On the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness occurs in the bladder and softening from cold and humidities, until it does not retain weak urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the back above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic area begin, and cauterize with one on the right of the back and another on the left of it: and let the length of that cauterization be according to the quantity of a knot of the thumb: and cauterize it with the lower iron of the back, or two irons if you judge it necessary for it: and let it be according to what has preceded, the cauterizing iron.
On the method of cauterizing the uterus.
When cold and humidities occur in the uterus, and it is prevented by that from impregnation, and its menses are corrupted, and the arrival of them is delayed, and pain occurs to it upon their arrival, then it is necessary to cauterize with three irons around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and cauterize above the lower part of the back with one iron, or two irons: and let the iron be a clavical one.
On the method of cauterizing the shoulder in dislocation.
When the mucus humors flow to the ankle of the ankle joint and become the cause of its exit from its place: and the sign of it is that one leg is longer than the other, when they are compared together: and the place of dislocation is found empty.
Therefore, it is necessary to cauterize the weak one above the ankle joint with a cautery similar to a circle: after you sign with a branding iron around the ankle joint, as it turns: and so that the ankle falls in the middle of the circle.
Which if this cautery is not present to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large olive-tree cautery: and let the depth of the cautery be according to the quantity of the thickness of the whole skin.
Then treat it, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for sciatica.
When pain occurs in the ankle joint and its causes are cold and humidity: and the weak one is treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not work, and it becomes chronic: then it is necessary to release the weak one from gross humors with fetid pills, or with artificial pills, and similar things. Then cauterize him.
And the method of the cautery in it is according to two methods: either a cautery with burning medications, or a cautery with fire.
The cautery with fire is according to many methods.
Of which one is, that you cauterize above the ankle joint with three triangular cauteries, according to this shape. And give them a good or bad depth. And let the space that is between all cautery be of the quantity of the thickness of a finger, and let the cautery be of olive oil.
Sometimes, however, the cautery is made in the middle on top of the head of the ankle itself. There are four cauteries.
And if you use a cautery with a circle, whose form precedes the dislocation of the ankle, alone: so that it is a little circle containing the whole ankle.
And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of cautery for sciatica, when the pain adheres to the ankle itself, and does not extend to the hip and thigh.
If it extends to the hip and thigh, then cautery it with two cauteries above the hip, above the place to which the weakness points, in which is the pain, and your cautery above the haunch four fingers towards the wooded part for a little while: and let the cautery be knife-shaped.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
What if the weakness indicates that the pain extends nearly to the toes of the foot, then cautery it there where it points with a cautery of one, two, three, or four, or more points, if it needs that.
And if it indicates the pain is under the knee turning to the thigh, then cautery it there with one knife-shaped cautery.
And beware to yourself in every cautery that you do, that you do not apply the cautery so as to burn a nerve, or a large artery, and draw out through it above the weakness a malignant tumor, or a contraction.
And I indeed have already seen one and another, of those who were cauterized above the haunch, and finished in the cautery, and the thigh became inflamed, until a tumor followed to the foot, and it was entirely perforated, and the entire foot was corrupted: thereafter there occurred a dissolution of the belly, and death after that.
What if there is pain in both parts at the same time, cauterize each according to this method.
And certain wise men have said regarding cauterization of the ankle, that this is the method of its cauterization. Make a similar iron instrument, the diameter of which is half a palm, and at its orifice it should be as thick as a kernel of a date, or a little less, and inside that instrument let there be a third instrument.
And let the space that is between all the instruments be the size of a thumb knot, and let the instruments be open on both sides, and let their height be like a knot, or two knots, and make for them a handle from iron decently fitted to the instruments.
Then let it be ignited in the fire until it becomes red and throws off sparks: then let it be placed on a weak ankle lying on its side. Cauterize it therefore with three round cauterizations in one spot.
Then leave it for three days. Afterwards apply a plaster with butter, and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasis said, we have used this kind of cauterization little, on account of the terror of its appearance, and because we find few who expect benefit from it.
However, it is one of the good cauterizations for whoever endures it and finds its place.
The cauterization with adhering medicines is like this, that you make two instruments having a perforated armlet, into which descends a hinge of its door made from bronze or iron, the length of a wall, of which in height are two knots, or about that size.
And let the space that is between both be the size of a finger's thickness, and let them be open at top and bottom, and let what they contain be joined together according to this form.
Then remove it and place it on a plaster of anchusa, while the patient lies on their healthy side. And press your hand strongly on the plaster of anchusa. Then pour between the two circles from warm water, which has been heated with fire for a short time, and hold it for an hour's space of time: and let the patient tolerate its biting and burning, for he finds the biting as fire, until the biting calms.
Then lift your hand with the instrument, and wipe away the warm water from the entire anchusa with sweet water: then leave it for three days.
And put on it butter, until the blackness of the burning is removed: and leave it for several days, and an ulcer will be cured from it. It is indeed the last resource in treatment.
Then treat it with ointments, until it heals.
What if the pain extends to the hip or the leg: make for him a plaster that contains water, according to what you did with the anchusa equally.
And this is the method of warm water: and I have already written it in the treatment of rectification of medicines. Take of alkaline substance and unslaked lime, both one part: grind each, and put them in a new pot, the lower part of which is perforated with one small hole, according to the quantity that the radius may enter: and put under the bottom of the pot another pot vitreous: and throw on the alkaline substance and lime from sweet water, so that it submerges both with your finger: after which you press them with a good compression by your hand: and leave the pot until the sharp water descends to the lower part of the vitreous pot.
Then collect that water entirely, and throw it on another lime: and filter, until it is renewed.
It will then be strongly active, which is administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of the remaining members. Because it performs the operation of fire itself.
And there are medicines with which they cauterize the ankle, such as these: tessie and mel of anacard, and chalk with soap, so that both are mixed together.
And Galen told of a certain ancient cure of some man, by which the pain of the ankle and the vein of the thigh was cured: and he declared its value to be great. And he said that it did not require another cure, and that he was healed by one remedy, until he told that he perhaps entered a bath of medicine, and came out of it already healthy.
And it is, that it be taken from the green of the seatragi, and if the green is not found, let the fresh and dry one be taken, and let it be ground much with some fat, and placed on the ankle, where there is pain, or on the leg, or on the hip: and let it be tied, and left for the quantity of three hours, or as long as he feels a weak sensation of burning. Then put him into a bath.
When therefore his body becomes very moist, put him into the sun. For the pain recedes and he is healed.
And know that it is not necessary to use a cautery with these medicines, unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides said that the dung of capers, when with it the vein of the thigh is cauterized, helps it: and makes a cautery in this manner. Let wool be ground, and imbued with old oil, and placed on the deep place, which is between the thumb of the foot, and the heel, and is closer to the heel.
Then take dry dung of a goat and set it on fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on a woolen cloth and let it stay until it is extinguished. Then repeat that. Do not stop doing that until the sensation is felt up to the knee and the pain subsides.
And this method of cauterization is called the cow-pox cauterization.
On the cauterization of pain in the back.
When pain occurs in the back for many reasons, or from a fall, or a blow, or from excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and wet material: and cauterization is not suitable, except in this single case, which occurs from the infusion of cold material.
It is necessary therefore after evacuation to apply to the weak person with foul-smelling poultices, and similar things, so that they make on the back, where there is pain, three lines according to the width of the affected part, afterwards marking with a cautery iron in each line five cauterizations, or more according to the quantity which can be tolerated by the strength of the weak person: and let the cauterization be done with cauterized points.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauterizations, with a cautery iron in the middle of the shoulder, according to this method.
On the method of cauterizing for the disease of gibbosity of the nape of the neck.
This sickness often happens to little children.
And the sign of this disease in children is: that there occurs a narrowing on the breath during elevation and movement: and you find in the upper part of the spine of the back and its knobs, which already begins to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When I raise that and make it thus, then cauterize it with a cauterizer which is a circle in this form.
And let the cauterization take hold equally over every part of the vertebrae: and if you cauterize around the vertebrae with a pointed cauterizer two or three lines: and let the points be close to one another.
Then treat the place until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware, lest you apply the cauterization on a hump that forms in the spasm of a nerve.
On the method of cauterizing for gout and pains of the joints.
When the pains of the joints are from cold humidities, which flow to whichever members of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is by custom of physicians to call that specifically Gout.
When therefore a cold gout is being treated with methods of treatment and the pains are not removed, then cauterization removes them.
And it is that you should cauterize it after evacuation around the joint of the foot with many cauterizers: and let the cauterization be with an oil.
And if you indicate that there are points on the surface of the foot, then make them with a pointed cauterizer. Which if the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize it on every knee with three cauterizers, or four on every side, with this same cauterizer of the ankle.
If however many of these cauterizations are necessary for you, then cauterize it. And do not insert your hand with the cauterizer, but rather to the thickness of the skin only.
If however the pains ascend to the knees and the back, then administer what we have said from the cauterizer in its chapter.
What if there are pains in the hands only, then punctures around the focus, as two lines revolve.
If however pain remains in the fingers, then puncture them, a point above each knot, and above the palm of the hand.
If however pains ascend after days to the elbows or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from every part.
And do not evacuate the weak from a good regimen, from the reception of medicines. For if a good regimen is made, and the phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with the aid of God by this cauterization.
On the method of cauterizing in cases of rupture.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestine descends, or a hernia to the testicle, and it is beginning nearby: then it is necessary to advise the weak person to omit purging on that day. And let him use laxatives, so that feces may descend from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and command him to hold his breath, until it comes out, or the hernia or intestine appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with a cauterization under the rupture above the bone of the hip, with a sign whose extremities are similar to the middle of a circle towards the upper parts of the body.
Then ignite the cauterium, which is of this form, until it becomes white, and throws out sparks. Then reduce the intestine or hernia to its concavity. Then let the servant place his hand over the spot, so that the intestine does not come out: and you have already opened between the thighs of the weak person, and put a cushion under it, and one servant holds the thighs of him, and another holds his chest who holds the hands.
Then apply the cautery on that same sign, your hand with the cautery standing upright. And hold it, until you have obtained a mouth with it, or repeat it with it twice or thrice, if you have not succeeded with it at first even unto the mouth.
And carefully observe from the exit of the intestine at the time of your cauterization, lest you burn it, and an issue comes out through that above the weak part or a sore or great evil.
And know that when you do not succeed with the cautery to the mouth, your operation is of no use.
And it is proper that the cautery for infants be subtle, according to their measure.
Then treat with the remaining ointment, until it has healed.
And let the weak person lie on his back for forty days, until the wound is closed.
And it is proper that you put nourishment for it for the length of time of its cure, which will soothe its stomach, so that the intestine does not come out at the anus and vomiting.
Then when he wants to get up after forty days, then administer a well-made bandage, and let him hold it for forty more days.
And he should be kept from labor, and from fullness of food and drink, and vehement voices.
For when he uses this regimen, thus he is healed with a complete healing.
And I will speak of the cure for hernias with an incision in its own chapter.
When however hernias occur in the remaining belly, and are beginning, and it is not possible to add them, then cauterize the hernia with a round cautery according to its quantity: and let that which is applied be about one third of it. Then treat it with what we have said, and it will not increase.
And some of the first ones have already said that a hernia should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is marked with a cautery, and a line is applied which runs along the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And put your hand in the middle with the cautery on the clavele.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
On the method of cauterizing for pains resulting from a fall or a blow.
Chapter 48.
When pain occurs in certain limbs from a fall or blow, and the pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines is not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize with a puncturing cautery.
And let the cautery be for each limb a second cautery according to its size, and its own slightness, and weakness, and its own power, and the location of the twisting and pain from it.
If therefore it is healed by the first cautery, it is good. If not: then repeat it over the same cautery.
Since it is customary with these pains that they are transferred from one limb to the one that is nearest to it. Wherefore it is necessary to follow them with a cautery until the weak part is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for leprosy.
Lepers are sometimes helped by a large cautery. And especially the type of leprosy which occurs due to the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: when therefore you consider treating it with a cautery.
If therefore the leprosy is beginning, and you have treated it with what we said in the division, and it does not decline, nor does it remain: and you apply above the weak part which comprehends the corruption above the entire complexion of it: then cauterize him above the head with five cauteries: one on the middle knot of the head, and a second below that towards the front at the end of the hair, and two above the two horns, and one behind above the nape of the neck.
And finally put your hand with the cautery briefly, until it impresses a small impression on the mouth, and the cortices will be dislocated from it: so that the expiration of gross vapors is alleviated from it, and cauterize with the cautery also over the spleen itself, according to what has preceded.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the weak part, and appears manifestly: then it is necessary to cauterize with those cauteries that we mentioned in the head, and to cauterize over the extremity of the nose, and with two cauteries over the two jaws, and with two cauteries over the vertebrae of the neck, and six over the vertebrae of the back, and one large one over the prominence near the tailbone and one over it, in the same alumead: and two over the shoulders: namely one over each shoulder, and two over the knees: one over each knee, and two over the shoulders, and two over the elbows, and two over the tenderness of its chest: and cauterize over every joint, of the joints of its hands and feet: and cauterize over every heel of its feet, and the soles of its hands.
And beware for yourself of the nerves that are above the posterior part of the heel, so that you do not burn them.
And when a cauterization is made with a cautery over the bone of the breast, and another over the bone of the stomach, and another over the liver.
And know that the more you apply the cautery, the greater is the benefit, and the more it helps.
And know that the weak person does not find pain in the cautery, as the healthy ones do: because his body is already numbed.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of a size and smallness according to the limbs and joints: according to what has preceded regarding the types of iron instruments.
Then treat with a cautery made from the powder of the herb with honey, and the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in cases of Gangrene.
When any limb is affected with gangrene and is treated with medicines, and oils, and plasters, and is not healed, then cauterize the affected limb with cauteries, according to what the size of the limb deserves or its smallness.
And let your cautery penetrate into the thickness of the skin for a short time. Then treat it with an ointment, until it is healed.
And when the gangrene is cauterized on that which occurs to the hand and foot, at the joints of the back near the exit of the nerves, which move that limb: and the numbness is removed.
But it does not presume above that, except for one who is wise in the anatomy of the limbs and the exit of the nerves moving the body.
Chapter 51.
When Barbers itch becomes chronic and nothing from the resources of medicine is effective for it: then cauterize over it with a deep cautery for a short time, according to the quantity of the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then treat it with the powder of the herb and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and pigeon's blood, and dove's blood: let each be one part: mix all these things, and apply them to a cloth, and adhere to the place, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for a Cancer.
When a cancer is beginning and you wish to restrain it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its circumference, as it revolves.
The wise men have said that it should be cauterized with a final cauterization in the middle.
It does not seem to me, for I fear that it will become an ulcer, and I have already seen that happen many times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around its circumference with a circle, as we have said, or with many cauterizations.
On the method of cauterizing in cases of scalding.
When someone has a scald and it is delayed in maturing, either because of the excess that causes it or because of the age of the weak person when he is decrepit and has little blood, or because of the time and the need to hasten the maturing of the scald, then cauterize around its circumference with many small points. Then leave it alone. For it will hasten the maturing by itself.
If you want to make a perforation of it with a cauterization iron, then ignite the cauterization iron, whose shape is this.
And place it in the middle of the scald, until it penetrates the skin: and let the cauterization be from that which follows, that the flow of pus may be relieved.
Then treat it until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for a corrosive ulcer.
Chapter 54.
A corrosive ulcer is nothing but a corruption that walks in a member and corrodes it: just as fire consumes dry wood.
