And the signs by which it is known where the collection of water is, are these. For if it is in the white membrane which we mentioned, then the swelling is round in length for a while as the figure of an egg: and the testicle does not appear, because the humidity contains it from every side.
And if it is humidity in its own proper membrane, then the swelling is round with part of the egg, and because of this a man thinks that it is another egg.
And if the humidity is between the skin of the testicles and the white membrane, then it falls under the sense.
When therefore you use the knowledge of the color of the humidity, then try the color of the humidity in the swelling with a probe that is inserted, whose shape has been described. Secondly, I consider what comes out in the wake of the instrument that has been inserted, and I judge it by what is between it.
When we proceed to cure with iron, then it is necessary that you should prescribe to the weak, that they should be bled if possible, and you see his body full.
Then he should be made to lie on his back on a high seat or bench, and many cloths should be put under him.
Then sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on his right side, who should stretch out the vein to one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles, and to the region of the navel.
Then take a broad spatula, and cut the skin of the testicles in the middle along its length, almost to the pectine: and let the incision be according to rectitude equidistant from the line which divides the skin of the testicles, until it reaches the white cord that encompasses: and pare it and observe, or beware lest you cut from this, as you cut it: and your paring should be where it hangs with the egg more: and carefully examine with the paring according to the quantity that is possible for you.
Then puncture the full cord with a wide perforation, and extract all the water.
Then separate between the two lips of the incision with forceps, and stretch the cord upwards, and do not touch the skin of the testicles that encompasses: and cut the cord as much as it is possible for you to cut it, either in its entirety or bit by bit, especially the wide part subtlely. For if you do not carefully examine, in the cutting of it there will be no security, lest the water return.
But if the egg proceeds outward from its skin during the time of your operation: then when you have completed the cutting of the cord, push it back. Then bring together the two lips of the skin of the testicles with a suture.
Then treat it as the rest of the wounds, until it heals.
What if you find a corrupted vein from blackness of another, then it is necessary to tie the vessels, which are the suspensors, fearing a flow of blood.
Then cut off the testicle with its suspensor, and extract the vein: afterwards treat it with what we have said.
If water is collected in the two parts, then know that there are two channels: cut therefore one part equally as you did in the other.
And if it seems to you that it is one operation, then do it: afterwards wipe away the blood. And insert into the incisions a thread soaked in oil, or in rose oil: and put on top another thread which you have soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over the two testicles, and the navel: and put on top of that double cloths, and they are bandages: and tie them on top with a ligature, which has six according to this form.
Then let two cloths be taken, and they be sewn, and filled with medicated wool, according to this likeness: and let extremities be made which are pressed from a cloth, or a wet thread: and let them be tied with a bandage around the loins of the arms: and one extremity take above the groin up to the back, and the second take at the part of the chest: and two extremities above the two hips below, and two other extremities above the two groins, and all the bandage be tied around the loins of the arms.
And when the ramex is artificially treated with a cautery in place of the incision with iron: and it is, that you take a small knife-shaped cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles with it: and it is ignited, according to what we have described: until when it is discovered that there is an album containing water: then take the cautery, according to this form.
It becomes like Greek poultices.
Then pierce that spongy flesh with it and it is cauterized until all the moisture goes out.
Then stretch the spongy flesh with forceps, and scrape it with a sharp burning cautery, and cut it according to what is possible for you, until you eradicate all of it.
And cauterize from the egg, so that the fire does not touch it.
And know that this operation is safer and less bloody and better than the operation with cutting.
If indeed it shows opposition to you at the time of cutting, or at the time of cauterization, a hot aposteme, or a flow of blood, or something else, then it is necessary that you should cure what shows opposition to you from that with a cure that suits it, according to what has been said before.
If however he is weak and fearful, and does not hope for this operation, because of its dreadfulness: then administer the piercing according to what I describe it to be.
When it is certain to you from what we have said concerning the signs, that the humor is watery: then it is necessary that you should make the weak person sit on an elevated seat.
Then pierce the aposteme in its lower part with a broad spatula, and make the piercing according to the length of the body, and let it be widely open, until all the water flows out.
Then put a dressing on the place, and bind it, and leave it so that the remainder of the water can flow out: then treat it until the wound is healed.
If however there is an obstruction to the flow of water at the time when you pierce it, and it does not happen except because the white pannicle makes an obstruction at the mouth of the wound, and prevents the exit of the water: then it is necessary that you should insert a feather into the wound, or an instrument with which the water of dropsy is extracted, whose form I previously described: or add to the operation of the wound for a little while.
And you should know that water returns and accumulates after six months, or around that time. When therefore it has accumulated, then it will perforate according to the same method, and the weak days will pass.
Chapter 63.
On the treatment of a fleshy ulcer.
You should know that in the operation on this ulcer, there is a risk of destruction due to fear in many conditions. Wherefore it seems to me that its dismissal appears to be beneficial for its healing.
And I recall an operation on it, and the appearance of a postule or boil.
I say therefore, that many boils occur in the bodies, from which the testicles are composed: and it happens for many reasons, namely.
Or from an excess of sharp or sour humors, which flow to the testicles. Or from a blow.
And the color of the boil is according to the color of the body, and no pain is found in it: and it is a serious boil.
And perhaps it is a stone boil, whose color is dark, and there is no sensation in it.
And sometimes it happens from the knotting of the arteries, and their swelling: as I have already mentioned before: or from the swelling of the veins.
That which is therefore from the swelling of the arteries, is recognized by the condition of the boil, when you press it with your fingers. And it is not necessary that you touch it directly.
That which happens from the swelling of the veins, does not disappear with pressing on it with the fingers.
And now it is possible that an operation be performed on this type, and on the rest of the flesh: and it is to cut the skin of the testicles. Then stretch the cord upwards, and extract it with a curved needle: and free the suspension from the vessels, and tie the vessels: and cut the suspension afterwards when you have freed it from every part of the cord.
If then the consolidated wound is with those born tissues, then it is necessary that you attract the wound and cut into it.
And if the adhesion is between something of the siphac, or in that which is between the vessels: then it is necessary that you free the whole of that adhesion, and cut into it with a rounded incision.
If however the nativity of the flesh is in the place of adhesion which is behind: then it is necessary that you cut the whole of it, and extract the wound, as we have said.
When therefore your operation is completed, then fill the wound with wool steeped in rose oil and wine: afterwards cure it with the remainder of the treatment, until it is healed.
Chapter 64.
On the treatment of varices, which is with a ligature.
A hernia is an unreduced protrusion with a certain reduction, similar to a botrus, with softening of the testicles: and it makes difficult the motion and exercise and walking of the infirm.
And in the cure of this disease is fear, on account of that which has preceded, the memory of it.
It is necessary that we say the operation in it according to what the first ones did.
I say therefore, that it is necessary that you make the infirm person sit on a raised seat. Then apply a suspender to the testicles towards the lower parts. Then hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, with vessels which are near the virgin area: and let another assistant hold them, and stretch them with a violent stretching.
Then cut with a broad sharp spatula a transverse section in the direction of the vessels, until the vessels are laid bare.
Then scratch from every part, as we have said to you in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples.
Afterwards fix on them a double thread where there is a filament, and tie it in the first places to which the veins arrive: and tie it again in the last of them. Then cut them in a straight cross-section according to the length of the body, and extract what is gathered from fetid corrupt humors.
Then treat the wound with the treatment of other wounds, in which a force is generated to produce a sanative, so that the vessels which nourish one of the testicles fall away. For it is not an evil on account of that.
And if the vein happens to all the vessels, then it is necessary that the testicles with the vessels be extracted on account of this: so that the egg is not deprived of nourishment, on account of the incision, and withers, or dries up, and is not a help with them.
Chapter 65.
Of the treatment of intestinal wounds.
The exit of this wound is from a section, which happens in the sifac extended over the belly in the groin area from the middle of the belly.
Why the intestines protrude from that rupture to one of the testicles. And this rupture is either from the sifac or from its extension.
And these two kinds happen from many causes: either from a blow, or a jump, or a shout, or the lifting of a heavy thing, and similar things.
And a sign, when it is from an extension of the sifac. It is that which happens gradually over a long time, and does not happen suddenly: and it is an equal abscess on the surface as opposed to the depth: because the sifac compresses the intestine.
And a sign of it when it is from a section of the sifac, because it causes to happen from the beginning a vehement pain suddenly: and it is a diverse abscess, appearing under the skin nearby: and that is on account of the exit of the intestine, and its course to the exterior of the sifac.
And when it comes out with the intestine a piece: and this is called intestinal Ramex and zirbium: and when it happens with inflammation.
And when feces run into the intestine and are retained there: and it is with them a danger to the weak: because it causes severe pain to happen, and especially when it is pressed.
And in the cure of the species of this disease with iron there is fear: where it is necessary to beware of the case in it.
And the method of treatment is, that you instruct the weak person, to reduce the intestine with his hand to the innermost parts of his concavity, if it has slipped back. Then he should be lifted up over his neck between your hands: and his thighs should be elevated.
Then stretch the skin that follows the skin to the upper parts, and cut the skin of the testicles along its entire length. Then fix on both lips of the incision hooks, according to which you will open the incision with them: and the incision should be according to the quantity that is possible, so that the egg can come out from it.
Then scratch the siphac, and what is under the skin of the testicles, until when the white sifach is revealed, hard on every side: then insert your index finger into that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white sifach, which is under the skin of the egg, and between the first and second sifach, and release with it the adhesion which is in the posterior part of the egg.
Then move with your right hand to the interior skin of the testicles: and with this extend the white sifach upwards, with your left hand: and lift the egg with the sifach to the part of the incision: and instruct the assistant, that he should stretch the egg upwards: and you solve the adhesion, which is behind the complete solution.
And search with your fingers, so that there is not anything there inside the intestine involved in the sifak, against the hard white thing. If you find something coming out of it, then push it to the lower abdomen.
Then take a needle, in which is a thick thread, made from ten threads: and insert it at the end of the sifak, that is, of the tunic, which is under the skin of the testicles which follows the section: then cut the extremities which stick out from the thread, until there are four threads. Then arrange some of them over others with a figure that is in the shape of a cross: and tie them with the sifak, which we spoke of, which is under the skin of the testicles with a violent ligature, until it cannot send anything from the vessels that nourish them to them: so that there does not occur from it a hot aposteme. And put again a second ligature outside the first ligature, at a distance from it less than two fingers. And after these two ligatures, let out from the sifak, which is under the skin of the testicles, a quantity of the size of a finger: and cut the rest entirely around the circumference, and remove the egg.
Then cut in the lower part of the skin of the testicles at the incision, from which runs blood and pus: as we have described in what has been said before.
Then administer a thread soaked in oil, and put it on the wound: and administer the ligature that we described. And sometimes cauterize the white sifak that we mentioned, after the incision of it, fearing a flow of blood. For this often happens. And let go the ligature until it falls off by itself.
If however the case is delayed, then moisten it with warm water: and put on it what we said, until it falls off.
Then treat the wound with the remaining treatments for wounds, until it is cured.
Chapter 66.
Of the stitch with the thread.
In this suture I have not seen anyone who has dared to undertake its cure with iron.

Chapter 67.
Of the hernia that occurs in the groin.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the area protrudes, and nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles: and if it does descend, it is very little, and returns every hour: but if it is prolonged with that time, a fissure is added in the sifach, until the intestines descend into the sifach.
And this occurs due to the extension of the sifach, which is in the groin, as we have said. Which is, that the sifach extends: then it becomes soft, and the area becomes inflamed, and protrudes.
And its treatment is with a cautery, as the description of it has preceded.
And sometimes it is treated with iron, in this manner: and it is, that the weak person lies on his back between your hands. Then cut the area of the ruptured and swollen place, a crosswise incision, according to the quantity of three fingers.
Then tie the alsifak and what is under the skin, until when the white sifach is revealed, which is under the skin that follows it.
Then take a scalpel and place it on the prominent area of the spleen and press it to the depth of the belly.
Next sew two prominent areas on the extremity of the scalpel from the spleen and connect one to another with a suture: then pull out the extremity of the scalpel.
And do not cut the spleen at all, nor stretch a vein, nor anything else, as I have made you know in the treatment of intestinal rupture.
Then treat it with the treatment of wounds. When you cut the threads, clean it, and restore the wound, until it becomes consolidated.
For the spleen contracts itself, and the prominence of the rupture is not added to.
And cauterization is better in this place: because it is closer to health.
Chapter 68.
On the softening of the skin of the testicles.
The skin of the testicles often becomes softened in certain men, because of which the flesh that is between them becomes softened and their appearance becomes disfigured.
Therefore it is necessary for he who is asked to cure it, to make the weak one lie on his back, and to cut away all the skin that has been softened from the natural skin.
Then bring together the two lips with a suture: and if necessary, or at first, the excess of softened skin with three or four sutures, and secure the suture.
Then cut between the sutures.
Then treat it with the treatment of other wounds, until it is healed, and the threads fall out.
Chapter 69.
On Castration.
Know that castration is forbidden by our law: and because of this, it would be permitted for me not to mention it in my book: and it is not necessary to mention it, except for two reasons.
One of them is that it should be in the science of the physician when he is questioned about it, and that he knows the cure for the one to whom it happens.
And another method is that we often need to castrate certain animals because of our needs through them, such as rams, boars, and cats, and similar ones among the animals.
I say therefore, that castration is done in two ways. Or by pulling. Or by tearing and cutting.
In that which is done by pulling, the method of operation is this: we make the animal sit in hot water until its testicles become soft and relaxed, and hang down: then we pull them with our hand until they are torn apart and do not appear to touch.
In castration by tearing and cutting, it is necessary that you hold the animal, and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the suspensory, and cut above all one ovum with a single section, until when two ovum proceed: then cut it after you have excised both, and do not leave on them anything of the sifaket except subtle sifac, which is above the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than that which is done by pulling: because pulling perhaps leaves something of the testicles, for which reason the animal desires copulation.
Then treat the wound, until it heals.
Chapter 70.
On the treatment of a hermaphrodite of two kinds.
A hermaphrodite is from the members according to two methods. One of them is that which appears in the space that follows, or on the skin of the testicles, in that which is between the two testicles, a figure like a woman's vulva, in which there are hairs: and sometimes urine flows from that which is on the skin of the testicles.
In women there is one species, and it is the vulva of the woman above the breast like the testicles of a small man entirely, standing out to the outside: of which one is like the penis of a man, and two like the two testicles.
And the treatment of the three species, two from men and one species from women, is: that it is necessary to cut away the excess flesh until the impression of them disappears. Then treat them with the cure of remaining wounds.
In the second species of men, from which urine exits, which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment at all.
Chapter 71.
On the cutting of the labia and the prominent flesh in the vulvas of women.
The labia possibly grow over the natural part, until they become ugly and their appearance is offensive: and sometimes they are enlarged in some women so much, that they spread out like in men, and reach to the coitus.
It is necessary therefore to hold the excess of the labia with the hand or with a hook, and to cut: and not to go too far in the cutting, especially in the depth of the root, so that there does not occur a flow of blood.
Then treat it with the treatment of wounds, until it heals.
The flesh that arises is the flesh that is born in the opening of the uterus, until it fills it: and possibly it comes out to the exterior like a tail: and because of this some of the first call the disease a "tailed" disease. It is necessary therefore to cut it as we cut the labia, and to treat it, until it heals.
On the treatment of the Imperforate, which is the woman's vulva not pierced.
Chapter 72.
The incision is such that it should be a woman's vulva not perforated or it should be a small opening. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental is from a disease which has preceded it: and this itself is made either from flesh born added, or from sifach subtle, or from a clamp: and it is made either in the depth of the matrix, or in its sides, or in its upper part, or in its lower part: and it prevents coitus and impregnation, and childbirth, and perhaps it prevents menses.
And the recognition of it is made by the aspect of an obstetrician, if the obstruction is appearing nearby.
If however it is not apparent, then seek it with your fingers, or with a probe.
If however the obstruction is from subtle sifach, and it is near the two lips: then touch it, and break it apart.
And it should be that you put upon the two lips a poultice.
Then place your indexes of the two hands together, and let the woman be on her back with her thighs spread apart. Then stretch the two lips with force, until the subtle sifach is broken apart, and the obstruction is opened.
Then take a woolen thread, and soak it in oil, and put it on the place: and let the woman apply it every day, so that the place is not consolidated with another vice.
If however the sifach is thick and dense: then it is necessary to cut it with a spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
If however the obstruction is from flesh born, then suspend it with hooks, and incise it: and let there be with you medicines which quiet the flux of blood without biting, such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and thus aggregated with the whites of eggs.
Then administer a lead pipe wide enough, so that the wound does not consolidate quickly, hold it for some days: and administer a plaster made from dry flax, then let the rest of the treatment be done, until it is healed.
And when there is a birth of flesh in the matrix of the nativities, it is necessary that they be cut according to this method: since there is not an apostema which is cancerous, for the cancerous apostema that is in the matrix does not become contrary with iron at all.
Chapter 73.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, Athehelil, and red pimples on the vulvas of women.
Hemorrhoids are indeed openings of the veins, insofar as there runs out from them much blood continually.
When therefore hemorrhoids become chronic, they become thelil: and I have already spoken about the division of their types, and their signs: and I will say here which of them receive a cure, and which do not.
I say therefore, that hemorrhoids which are in the opening of the matrix and do not appear to the senses: then there is no cure for them with iron.
But those of them which are in the opening of the matrix and upon which the sensation falls, are those that can be cured.
It is necessary therefore that you put the woman into a cold house. Then stretch out the hemorrhoids with forceps or with coarse cloth, and cut them out from their roots.
Then sprinkle over them at the flow of blood from one powder of incisions without biting: such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense and similar things.
Then press her feet against a wall for one hour. Afterwards put her into cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, and a crust of pomegranates, and gall, and similar things.
Then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on her back.
If blood is cut off with it, it is good: and if not, make the ventoses adhere to the back and the breasts, without scarification.
Then take a wool and submerge it in the juice of tarathit, or the juice of arnoglossa, or the juice of the branches of alaulat, that is, aglanter, Pontic wine, and make it adhere to the place.
When then the aposteme quiets, treat the place with ointments, until it is healed.
The Albarth herb is similar to the heads of alhaasse, and its appearance is rough.
It is necessary therefore that you cut what appears from it, according to what I said equally in the former: and treat it, until it is healed.
Chapter 23.
Of the perforation of the uterus which occurs in the matrix.
There occur in the matrix many kinds of apostemes, such as cancer, and aposteme of stones, and ulcers, and adubelati, and alekilati, that is, herpes, aestiomemus, and fistulas, and hemorrhoids, and ragadiae, and thelil, and hot aposteme.
And I have already spoken of all these diseases and their kinds, and the signs of them, and their cures in division: it is necessary that I speak in this treatise of the hot aposteme which occurs in the matrix, when it is among the apostemes which collect blood, and you should know how its opening is done with iron.
It is necessary therefore that you consider. Then if the pain of the aposteme in its beginning is acute with its percussion, and inflammation, and fever: and you see it to be red: if sense falls upon it, then do not hasten with its perforation: and treat it with that which helps against maturation, until when the acuteness of the accidents quiets.
Then it is appropriate that you make the woman sit on a seat that has two seats, and she should lean back or lie on her back, and bring her feet to the lower part of her abdomen: and her hips should be expanded, and she should put her arms under her thighs, and tie them with a convenient ligature.
Then the midwife should sit on the right side, and administer the instrument by which the opening of the matrix is opened.
And it is necessary when you administer this instrument, that you fix with the radius the depth of the woman's matrix: so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the matrix, and hurts the weak part.
If the instrument is more than the depth, then it is necessary that you put pillows on the surface of the depth of the matrix: so that the entrance of the whole instrument into the depth of the matrix is prohibited: and it is necessary that a loop, which runs on the instrument, be placed from the upper side: and that it hold the instrument, and that the servant turn the loop, until the depth of the matrix is opened.
When therefore the exit appears, and is touched by the hand, and it is gentle and soft: then it is necessary that you cut it at its head with a broad spatula.
When therefore the sanies is evacuated, then it is necessary that you put on the wound a dressing submerged in rose oil: or green oil, in which there is a certain astringency: and put the dressing, and extract the section from the depth of the matrix.
And put externally on the matrix, and on the navel a clean woolen cloth submerged in water, in which mallows have been boiled.
Then it should be treated after two days with an ointment that is suitable for it, until it is healed.
And when the matrix and wound are washed, it is cleaned with water and honey; then with water in which the root of lily or long aristolochia has been boiled; then it returns to the ointment.
What if the wound is hidden within the matrix, then it is necessary that you prohibit the cure of it with iron, but rather cure it with what we have said in the division.
Chapter 70.
The doctrine of obstetrics, how they medically treat living embryos, according to an unnatural shape having emerged.
It is necessary for the obstetrician to recognize first the shape of a natural birth.
From the signs of it, is that when you see a woman compressed at the lower parts, and desires to smell the air, and there is relief over her what is over her from birth, and the exit of the embryo is hastened: then know that this birth is according to natural shape, and its exit is over its head, and the afterbirth with it: or suspended, or hanging from the navel.
When you see these signs, then it is necessary that her womb be compressed, so that the embryo descends quickly.
For when it descends over its head, the afterbirth descends with it, and is cleansed from those superfluities of a good cleansing.
Which however is beyond this birth, is unnatural, deserving no praise.
Since when the fetus exits over its feet, and its body exits before its head, and its feet, and one of its hands, or one of its feet: or its head and its hands exit: or its belly exits: and perhaps it is turned over its neck, and similar things from unnatural shapes.
It is necessary therefore for the obstetrician to be prudent, subtle in all these things, and beware of error and deception: and I am showing every shape from them, and how it is ingenious in it, and signified by that, and established upon it.
When the fetus moves up above its head with its natural exit, and presses upon the woman, and parturition becomes difficult for her, and you see her virtue now weakened: then make her sit upon a seat, or let women hold her: and apply vapors to her vulva with decocted fumitory, and with humid oils.
Then the Midwife should insert between her fingers a small spatula, and find with it the secondine, and cut it with her nail, until there runs out what is in it from humidity: and press the belly of the woman, until the fetus descends.
If however it does not descend, then it is necessary that the woman be given a clyster of fumitory mucilage, with sesame oil.
Then order her after the clyster, that she be compressed: and make her sneeze with condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour. For the fetus will come out immediately.
What if the two hands of the fetus come out first, then it is necessary that you reduce them with ease little by little. If however it does not enter at the entrance, then put the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up high: then strike the seat against the ground: and let the woman be held, so that she does not fall with the shock.
If therefore the hands do not come out, and the fetus dies: then cut them off, and extract the remainder of the fetus: and tie its hand with a cloth, and pull it out gently: for it will come out.
The fetus comes out over its feet. When the fetus comes out over its feet, then it is necessary that you push them up high: then turn the fetus little by little: afterwards pull it even.
Then take one of its feet and stretch it out little by little.
When the suppurating matter comes out up to the hips, then order him to compress it and make him sneeze with condiments: it will come out, if God wills.
And if it does not come out with what we have described, then reduce the fart little by little until you put it in its natural shape. For it will itself come out then with an easy exit.
What if it is prohibited with all that we have described: then take from the mucus of the altea, and oil of sisamine, and dissolved gum: and strike the whole in a mortar with a good stroke: then smear the woman's vulva and her lower belly. Then make her sit in warm water, until she obtains a hypogastric discharge.
When you see that her lower parts are already warmed, then make for her a seat of myrrh: and apply it. When she has held the seat for one hour, then make her sit on the seat. Then make her sneeze: and constrict its mouth and nose: and press the lower part of the belly with an easy compression. For the fart will come out immediately.
The fetus comes out over the knees and hands. When it comes out according to this form, then she should insert her hands gradually. Then the woman should be lifted up over her neck, and her feet hang down to the lower parts: and she herself should sit leaning on a bed, and clasp her hands. Then press above her belly little by little. Then extract what is under her feet from the dust, until it is prepared in the lower part. What if the fetus does not come out, then take her feet and move them with a vehement movement. Then press what is above the hypogastric region little by little, until the fetus ascends to the upper parts. Then he should insert his hands and gradually straighten the navel, and instruct the woman to press, until the fetus comes out.
The fetus hanging crosswise from the hands having exited. It will be kneaded during the reduction of his hands. If however he cannot reduce it, then let him lift the woman and make her walk.
If indeed she is not able to walk, then let him make her lie on a bed and strike her knees with a violent concussion.
Then administer the ointment that you have prepared from poultices.
Which if the afterbirth comes out, then make her sit on a seat. Then attend to the reduction with the hands, and straighten the fetus according to its natural shape: and make the woman sneeze, and instruct her to press herself, until it comes out.
The fetus exits with its head behind its shoulders, its hands stretched out, and its face towards the mother's back. It is necessary that the midwife should hold the hand of the fetus, then slowly turn it, and straighten it with ease.
When it is straightened, then put on its neck what we have prepared from oil and poultices.
Then instruct her to move it slowly. When you have done that, then make her sit on a seat, and instruct her to lean towards the right side. Then instruct her to press herself, and make her sneeze with coughing.
The prepared fetus exits on the side. When it descends to the opening of the womb in this manner with the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with your nail, until it is evacuated from the moisture.
If indeed it hangs over the face of the fetus and its neck, then cut it from the navel, so that it is not retained and does not cause death.
Then push the fetus to the inside, until you place it according to what is suitable, and instruct the woman to compress herself several times, for it will come out with an easy delivery.
The exit of twins, or a fetus of many. Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three and four are born. But truly that is extraordinary, and rarely happens.
Five is a thing beyond nature, and they do not live long: and the afterbirth contains them, however many they are multiplied, one secundine: and they are separated by a membrane, distinguishing between them the ligament at the navel of each of them.
And sometimes they come out just as one fetus comes out with a natural and easy delivery: and they come out with a laudable delivery, as we have described.
That if any of them are difficult at birth, and they reach that which we spoke of concerning unnatural positions, then treat them as we have described: and let it be by a subtle hand, and do what is done with ease and slowness, and it will be adapted according to every figure with what is prepared for it from the guiding intellect towards health.
The memory of that which is formed in the womb from embryos, and are aborted.
Sometimes one is formed in the womb, and two, and three, and four, and five, and six, and seven, and more than ten: and it has been verified by me, that a woman, aborting, expelled seven, and another fifteen, all formed.
Which was done by the measurement of the glorious wise one.
This therefore is all that is required to be in the science of Obstetrics. Perhaps indeed he will come across something similar to that: so let him oppose it with what is suitable.
Chapter 76.
On the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus with what I mentioned in the division from medication, and it does not come out, and you are compelled to use an operation with the hand, then it is necessary that you consider.
If the woman is of healthy strength, and is not with any of the accidents, from which loss is feared for her: then it is necessary that the woman be placed on a bed, on her back, and her head be inclined downwards, and her thighs be elevated: and an assistant hold her from both sides, or she be tied to the bed, so that her body not be moved during the extraction of the fetus.
Then the mouth of the matrix is moistened with humid oils of linseed, and flax, and fenugreek.
Then the midwife anoints her hand with these oils and mucilages: then she inserts it into the matrix with ease. Then she feels for the place where the nails will be fixed from the fetus, and the places convenient to it.
Consider then, if the fetus is prepared to descend on its head: then fix the hooks in its eyes, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or in its palate, or under its beard, or in its throat, or in places near the ribs, and under the hips.
If however it descends on its feet, then in its chest, and in the middle of its ribs.
And it is necessary that she hold the hook with her right hand: and put the curvature of it between the fingers of the left hand: and insert it with ease, and fix the hook in one of those places which we mentioned, until she reaches the empty space.
Then fix another hook or a third if necessary, opposite to it: so that the contraction be equal, and not decline to one side.
Then it should be extended with an equal extension, and the extension should not be according to straightness only, but rather it should be moved to every part, so that its exit is alleviated, just as it is done with a tooth during its extraction.
And it is suitable for what is between them, that the extension is softened. What if a part of it is retained, then it is necessary that the midwife anoints some fingers with oil, and inserts them from the side, so that she delivers with them what is retained.
If therefore a part of the fetus comes out, then the hooks are moved to another place that is higher: do this until the entire fetus comes out.
If therefore the hand comes out before the other, and it is not possible to push it back, on account of its constriction: then it is necessary that a cloth is wrapped over it. Then pull it out until when the whole comes out, cut it at the joint of the foot, or at the elbow: and so it is necessary that you do to the other hand, and to the two feet.
If the head of the fetus is large, or it suffers constriction at the exit, or there is water collected on its head: then it is necessary that a spatula spinosa is inserted between the fingers, and finds with it the head, and extracts the water: or it breaks it with an instrument which is called Almisdac: whose shape comes with the shapes of other instruments in the chapter that follows this one.
Similarly, let it be done if the fetus is of a large head nature, then it is necessary that the shoulder is cut: or extract it with a misdach, as we have said. Then pull the bones with forceps.
What if the head comes out and is constricted at the fork: then it should be pierced until the moisture that is in the chest is poured out.
If it is not complicated and does not obstruct the exit, then cut the head bit by bit, according to what is possible for you.
What if the lower part of the abscess is apostemated, or there is dropsy in it: then it is necessary that you perforate it, until humidity flows out from it.
If the fetus is positioned over its feet, then its extraction is easy, and its direction to the mouth of the matrix is slight.
If it is constricted at the belly or chest: then it is necessary that you extract it with a cloth which you have wrapped over your hand: and press the belly or chest, until what is in them flows out.
If the other limbs are delivered, and the head returns: then the Midwife should insert her left hand. If the mouth of the matrix is open, then she should insert her hand into the depth of the matrix, and search for the head with it, and draw it out with her fingers to the mouth of the matrix: then she should insert one hook, or two hooks, into it, and draw it out with them.
What if the mouth of the matrix is constricted, on account of a hot apostema which has happened to it: then it is not necessary that she should labor over it, but rather it is necessary to administer an effusion of humid things, and apply plasters: and sit in waters which soften and moisten.
What if the fetus is on its side, then it is possible that it will equalize: then administer what we have said regarding a living fetus.
What if it is not possible, then cut bit by bit, and extract.
And it is necessary that you do not leave anything of the afterbirth inside at all.
When you have completed your operation, then administer what we have said regarding hot apostemas that happen to the matrices.
What if it happens there is a flow of blood, then let it descend into astringent liquids, and administer the remainder of the treatment.
And I have already seen a woman, in whose womb a dead fetus was: afterwards she became pregnant on top of it, then another fetus also died. It happened to her after a long time an abscess on her navel, and it became swollen, until it was opened: and it began to emit pus.
I was summoned therefore to her treatment, and I treated her for a long time: and the wound was not consolidated.
I placed therefore on it certain strong attractant plasters: and the bone came out from the place. Then several days passed for her, and another bone came out. I was astonished therefore at that, since there is no bone in the womb.
I thought therefore, that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
I probed the wound, and extracted many bones, with the woman being in her better conditions: and she lived for a long time afterwards, and a little pus came out from the place.
And I did not confirm this strange thing, except that there is science in it, and assistance for that which the skilled physician administers with his hand from treatment.
Chapter 78.
On the forms of necessary instruments for extracting a fetus.
The form of the Vertiginis by which the matrix is opened.
This below is the form of a Tightener, which has two equal arms, with two uprights at the ends of two wooden rods. However, this Upright should be finer than the Tightener: and that it be made either of ebony or of boxwood.
And the width of each wooden rod is about two fingers: and the thickness of each of them is about one finger, and the length of each of them is a palm and a half: and in the middle of the two rods there are two additions of the same kind of wood, which are already fixed to both, whose length is half a palm and a little more: and the width of each is about two fingers or a little more.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the matrix, so that it opens with them when you turn two Vertigines.
The form of another like that, more subtle and lighter.
Let it be made from ebony wood or boxwood, similar to the likeness of forceps. However, on the extremity of it there are two additions, as you see here above: and the length of all the addition from them is a palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
When you wish to open the matrix with it, then have the woman sit on a couch, her feet hanging down, with what is between her thighs open. Then insert these two additions joined together into the matrix, and you hold the extremity of the instrument below between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with forceps, equally according to the quantity that you wish from the opening of the mouth of the matrix, until the midwife does what she wants.
The form of another Vertiginis which the ancients called the form of the Impeller by which the fetus is pushed.
The form of the Almisdac, by which the large head is compressed: and it is similar to forceps, which has teeth on the extremity, as you see.
And sometimes it is made with a stop, like forceps according to this form, as you see, which has teeth like the teeth of a saw, by which it is cut and compressed.
The form of the Vncinus having one spike.
The form of the Vncinus having two spikes.
The spatula has two extensions for cutting off the head.
Shape of two broad Spatulas.
All these instruments are to be exercised, and the more their kinds are multiplied and prepared by the artisan, the swifter will be his operation and the higher he will be among men, on account of their quantity.
Do not therefore despise any of them, so that it may be prepared by you. Their necessity is indeed inexcusable.
Chapter Seventy-Eight.
On the extraction of the Secondine.
When the Secondine is retained with the afterbirth, then it is necessary that you should precipitate the weaker one, so that it may retain its breath. Then make it sneeze with a condiment: and press your hand over its mouth, and its nostrils. If then it comes out through this, it is good.
If not: then take a pot, and perforate in its cover an opening: and put in it herbs that open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, and dill, and chamomile, and sesame, and lignous cassia, and centaury: take all these herbs, or some of them, and submerge them with water, and put them over fire.
Then put a bulb of reeds over the opening of the pot, and another end into the mouth of the womb: and hold it until the vapour penetrates to the concavity of the womb.
Then make it sneeze, as we have said. For the Secondine will come out with facility.
If however it remains after this cure, and does not come out: then instruct the Midwife, that she should submerge her hand in oil of sesame, or mallow. Then he should insert it into the wound and look for the secondary wound with it. When therefore he has found it, then he should take it and pull it out gradually.
If it is attached deep within the womb, then he should insert his hand, as we have described, until when he finds the secondary wound, and pull it out gradually according to what is right, so that the womb does not fall during violent pulling: indeed it should be turned with ease to the right and left sides: then add to the amount of the pulling. For it detaches itself then, and is saved, and comes away from the adhering things.
What if the mouth of the womb is constricted, as we have already described: treat it with fumigation, and from a medication of a poultice with herbs.
If however it does not come out with all that we have described, then beware lest you weary yourself over it in the repetition of the extraction.
It is necessary indeed, that what comes out to the mouth of the womb from it, should be tied to the thigh of the woman. Then anoint her with the ointment tetrapharmacon. For it will rot it after some days, and it will dissolve, and will come out.
Truly when it rots, there rises from it a bad smell to the stomach and head, and it harms that weak woman. It is necessary therefore that fumigations suitable for that be administered.
Certain of the ancients have already experienced the fumigation of nasturtium and figs of sycar.
The form of an instrument with which a woman is fumigated for the retention of the secundina and menses.
Let a vessel be made similar to an alcama, or from clay: and let the wide end be placed over the fire: and let the fumigation be put on the coals: let her hold it, until that fumigation is consumed: and then another.
Chapter 79.
On the treatment of a non-perforated anus.
Many of the boys are born, and their anuses are not perforated, which the subtle siphac has already obstructed. It is necessary therefore, that the midwife should perforate the siphac with her finger: and if not, she should perforate it with a sharp style: and let her beware of the intestine, lest it touch it.
Then put on top of it a piece of wool soaked in wine and oil. Then treat it with ointments, until it is healed.
If however the time comes that it becomes obstructed, then put a lead pipe in the opening for many days, and it will be removed when the boy wants to defecate.
And now obstruction of the anus also occurs from the consolidation of a wound, or an abscess. It is necessary therefore that the consolidation be cut, then treated with what we have said concerning treatment and lead.
Chapter 80.
On the treatment of fistulas that occur in the lower part.
The fistulas that occur in the lower part are a knot and a thickness that occur near the anus of the fundament or in the space of one of the parts: and it is one fistula or several.
When therefore that knot becomes chronic, it opens, and a watery white humidity or subtle pus flows out from it.
And sometimes there are ones of these fistulas that penetrate. Therefore the penetrating ones are recognized by that which comes out from the bowel movement and flatulence, when the sick person uses the bowel movement: and perhaps worms come out from them.
And there are ones of these fistulas when they penetrate the space up to the bladder and up to the passage of the rod. And there are ones of them that penetrate up to the joining of the hip and up to the knot of the tail.
From that which is known, the penetrating fistula reaches to the anus, and also from the non-penetrating one, it is so that you insert your index finger into the anus, and you insert a subtle probe made of air or iron when there is no tortuousness.
What if there is tortuousness in it, then insert into it a subtle probe made of lead, or a horsehair, until you feel the probe or the hair on your finger.
What if you do not feel it deeply, nor does anything proceed from the orifice by way of excretion, nor wind, nor worm as I have said: then know that it is non-penetrating: proceed therefore to the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating to the bladder or to the urine passage: then its signification is the exit of urine from it, and its prohibition from this so that the place may be consolidated with medicines.
If it is penetrating to the hip joint or to the mouth of the hip: then its sign is that the probe penetrates up to that place, if there is no tortuousness up to the mouth: and the finding of pain in the surrounding part, and that pus always comes out from it: and that medicine is not effective in it, nor is it consolidated with ointment.
And in all these penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all: and the treatment of them is labor and vanity to him, from foolish medicines, on which it is formed.
In that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing is hoped for with a plaster: according to what I relate to you, and I have already proven: and it is, so that the weak person lies on his back between your hands, and you elevate his legs up above his hips, and his hips are inclined towards his belly. Then insert a lead or copper probe, if there is tortuousness in the fistula, until you know where the probe penetrates.
If however he feels it weak around the anus, then it is necessary that you insert your index finger into the anus.
If therefore you feel on your finger the probe having already penetrated by itself and detected, besides what you feel between your finger and the anus or flesh, then therefore you know for certain that it is penetrating: therefore do not labor in it, since its treatment is not like what we have said.
They have said, however, that the flesh is healed in some men and from the medication which is hoped for as a remedy, it is that you make a subtle cauterization according to the width of the Fistula, as was previously described, and insert the ignited thing into the Fistula until it reaches around the anus. Then repeat that two or three times, until you know that all those fleshy growths which are like the quill of a bird's feather have already been burned.
Then treat it with cloths wrapped in butter, until those growths that have been burned come out: then treat it with ointments that generate and consolidate flesh.
If therefore it heals, it is good.
And if not, then it does not heal with another cure of an ointment.
And if the probe comes out and has not reached up to your finger which is in the anus, and there is between it and the probe a thick covering of flesh or sifac: and you see the Fistula in that which follows the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the Fistula, and you direct the cutting with the probe that is in the fistula, until the cutting reaches where the end of the probe reaches, and the probe is freed and falls out.
Then clean those fleshy growths that resemble the quill of a bird's feather, so that none of them remain.
If however blood overcomes you, and it separates between you and your operation so that you cut those flesh: then what is done is better, and for the speedy healing, it is to cauterize it with fire, or with sharp medicine.
Since the cauterization with fire aggregates good habits, it adds to the burning of those flesh, and the cutting off of blood, and the drying of moistures.
Then treat it with liniments wrapped in butter, or with pounded cabbage, until the place emits pus, and the burned flesh goes out into the pus.
Then treat the wound with consolidating ointments, which generate hard flesh: and there are medicines in which there are astringents and drying.
For when it is restored, then already it is healed: and do not repeat the treatment.
If however the fistula has already perforated to the depth of the anus, and it is prolonged from the excess of body, then insert your finger into the anus, and examine with it.
If therefore you feel a tension, and between you and it there is a covering of sifac, or flesh, and it is near to the penetration: then there is no operation on that, except according to the way of confidence and hope.
Which is, that one of the three methods is administered in it: either that you cauterize it, as we have said: or that you cut it, until you obtain its concavity, so that it is possible for you to insert liniments, and a cure from nearby. And do not proceed far with the cutting, lest you injure the membrane that contains the anus, and it happens above the weak exit of the involuntary evacuation without control. Then treat it with what we have said.
Perhaps it will be healed: or you stretch the covering, and cleanse it after you cut it up to near the anus, as we have said, either with a probe, or with another instrument of sharp extremity. Then clean those filtered flesh parts that are in the incision, until where you can with scrutiny.
Then be concerned with the restoration of the entire wound with the incision, and the upper opening where it consolidates, and a remaining fistula open in the interior part of the anus, and it will be easier on the weaker.
And when a fistula follows in this manner: and it is, when you insert a probe into the Fistula: and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with skin and margin of the anus: then take the probe of the perforated extremity, which is like a needle, that is, preparing the tissues, according to this form. And insert into it a thread wound from five threads, and tie around it. Then insert the probe with the thread into the Fistula, until it reaches its concavity.
If then it is penetrating the margin of the anus internally near, then pull out the thread from that hole: so that you insert your finger into the anus, and pull out the end of the thread, and bring together the two ends: and tie both, and leave it for one day, or two days: and as much as the thread cuts into the flesh, tie it well, until the flesh that is between the two ends of the thread is cut, and falls: then treat the wound, until it consolidates, and heals.
If however the opening of the Fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrate by whatever method is prepared for you, unless it is deep within. For you should not do that on account of the pain, so as not to cut it.
Then do with it as we have said, until it is healed.
The shape of the spatula for a fistulous spine, which is found where the fistula is, whose curvature is sharp, and the other part is not sharp, so that it does not cut what is not necessary, as you see.
Chapter 81.
On the suture of hemorrhoids, from which blood flows from the incision of them: and the cure of fissures.
There are hemorrhoids in two modes. Either they are inside the anus, similar to vessels of charcoal, or of nuts: or as if they themselves were grain of a nut. And of them there are small ones, and large ones: and blood flows from them always, and it is one, and they are many. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
Truly however those that are outside the anus, are for the most part small in humidity, from which flows yellow water, or a little blood with constant flow: and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of that which is inside the anus, is that you should press on the weak one so that it slips out: and it is squeezed, until the anus comes out, and the threads appear to you. Therefore hang them with hooks: or hold them with your finger. Then cut them at their roots.
If however they are not retained by the hooks, on account of their humidity and softening: then take them with rough cloth, or with a napkin made from coarse wool, and extract them with your fingers. Then cut them, and powder over them after the incision certain hot powders, so that they may serve in place of a cauterization. Or cauterize them according to what was previously mentioned in the chapter on cauterizing. Then treat them with the remaining treatment, until they are healed.
Which if the anus does not obey for evacuation, then give a cluster of enema in which there is a little mordication, so that it may strike with what is in the anus, and it obeys evacuation quickly, when the weak one evacuates.
If however the hemorrhoids are extracted from the anus then their treatment is easy and simple and it is like you catch them with your finger or catch them with a hook and cut them. Then treat them with what we have said, until they are healed.
And whoever shuns cutting with iron, then it is fitting that you administer their suture according to this method. Take a thread and insert it into the needle. Then pull the hemorrhoid upwards and make it penetrate with the needle at its root from the other side: and tie the two ends of the thread on the lower part of the needle, and let them be crosswise: and constrict the hemorrhoid with a strong tightening. Then knot the thread and withdraw the needle.
Do this with all the hemorrhoids and leave one of them alone: nor let itself, so that blood flows out excessively from it.
Then put on the anus a cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate, and put it on the anus: and order the sick person to rest. Then leave it alone until it falls off.
When the hemorrhoids fall off, treat them with ointments and the remainder of the treatment, until they are healed.
Of the treatment of Fissures. For often it happens from dryness of the feces and constriction of the nature.
When they become old and medicine does not penetrate them: then it is fitting that you rub with the points of a spatula or with your finger until they become moist and the outer skin which prevents them from consolidating is removed. Then treat them until they consolidate according to what is fitting.
If however they do not consolidate: then rub them again with a more vehement rubbing than the first, until they bleed much, and afterwards treat them until they are healed.
On the treatment of inverted and non-inverted piles, and of hemorrhoids, and of fistulas.
Chapter 82
Know that Almirmar is nothing but a round knot according to the color of the body, similar to the head of a club: and it occurs in the whole body, especially in the lower parts of the feet, and toes: and pain happens from them during walking.
It is necessary therefore that what is around the club should be cut, and it should be held with forceps, or with a hook, and it should be eradicated from its root.
Then treat that: and if you want to cauterize it according to what was previously mentioned in its chapter.
From the dry hemorrhoids one is a small, rough, flat, round eminence on the surface of the body. And they often occur in the hands of children.
And the treatment of it is, that you should stretch the hemorrhoid, and cut it: or tie it with a silk thread: or with a probe, until it falls off. And if you want, cauterize it according to what was previously mentioned with fire, or with sharp medicine: and now both the inverted and non-inverted hemorrhoids are eradicated with an instrument that I will mention.
A boil is also a small, flat, thick elevation on the surface of the body, going deep into the flesh: and when it meets cold, it feels like the biting of a ant, and it occurs in the whole body: and most often it occurs in the hands.
And the treatment of it is, that you should take a small tube from a goose feather, or a strong vulture's feather: and put that tube over the boil, until the circle of the tube constricts its parts. Then move your hand with the tube, until you cut what is around the boil: and you put it deep into the flesh, and eradicate the boil from its root.
And if you use it, make that with a copper or iron tube, according to this shape.
Let the upper part of the tube be drawn to subtlety so that the thread wraps around it, so that the grasp of the finger is alleviated and its own rotation.
And if you use cauterization of ants according to what was previously mentioned in the cauterization of Athelil in the chapter on cauterization.
Chapter 83.
Of the forms of instruments which are administered for clysters in diseases of the anus, and for the relief of the belly, and for colic.
Sometimes the clyster is made from silver, or from gilt, or from copper, or from brass.
And sometimes it is made small and large from these instruments, according to those in which they are administered.
That which is administered in the treatment of little children should be small: and those whose anuses are weak, or painful, so also their clysters.
Large clyster.
The tube of it, that is, the upper head in which the string is tied, should be spacious according to this method: and it should have a distinction so that the string can be tied as you see, and the lower end which is inserted into the anus, should be smooth, that is, not open, gentle, very, drawn to subtlety: and on one side of it there should be two openings, and on the other side one opening.
And the width of the opening should be according to the thickness of the rods, and a little thicker, and there should be a string in which medicines are placed from the bladder of an animal: or from paper, which is according to the shape of a small asafoetida: whose root is one palm.
And it should be perforated with many openings as it revolves, and the space that is between all the openings should be the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those openings a strong thread made from coarse thread, which should be of ten threads or thereabout, and mix with it the wool like gum arabic. When therefore the wool is placed in it, a thread should be tied at its head between two distinguishing constrictions of the rectal clamp. Then tie the cluster with it.
And this is the form of the circle and the utensils depicted here, and of the openings.
The quality of tying with it, is that you fill the wool or the bladder with medicine, which should be warmed according to the quantity of the tolerance of the weak person: and beware lest it be very hot or very cold.
Then the weak person should be placed on his back and lift his thighs upwards: and put under him an inthan, that is, a skin upon which men sit, or a linen cloth.
Then anoint the extremity of the rectal clamp with oil, or with egg white, or with the mucus of the flax seed, or similar things. Then insert it into the anus with ease. Then the assistant should take the wool with both his hands at once, and squeeze it out with force, until he evacuates all that is in the rectal clamp into the intestine.
Then withdraw the rectal clamp, and let the weak person lift his thighs to his side.
If the medicine brings it to the end, then let him hold back as much as he can. And if he sleeps with it the whole night, it is more beneficial for the treatment.
If however you administer it to him in diseases of abdominal flux, and its evacuation is hastened: then repeat the rectal clamp until he is cured.
If there are hemorrhoids or painful boils in the anus, then let the rectal clamp be very subtle, gentle, from those rectal clamps with which children are treated.
And this should be the form of a subtle enema on which the skin is tight.
Head, 84.
I have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds that which pertained to the book, and I will say here the treatment of them with the hand, and with medicines according to completion.
I say therefore, that wounds are diversified according to that by which the wounds are made, and according to the place on which the wound falls.
The things by which wounds are made are often such as the throw of a stone, or the cut of a sword, or the blow of a cudgel, or the thrust with a spear, or a stick, or an arrow, and similar things to these many.
The wounds which are made according to the places of the body are, such as a wound that falls on the head, or neck, or chest, or belly, or liver, and similar ones from these members.
And I am telling the treatments of certain wounds, so that I may put that reasoning and rule on the remaining wounds.
And I will begin with simple head wounds, since the discussion of compound fractures will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
I say therefore. When there is a simple wound on the head and it is not a fracture of bone: consider then if it is from the throw of a stone, or similar things, and has only broken the skin: and it is a great wound, and you apply on top a warm poultice for an aposteme: then do bloodletting at once, and do not delay it: and take out from the blood according to the quantity of its virtue: if there is nothing that prohibits bloodletting, especially if the blood which comes out of the wound is little. And let bloodletting be from the opposite side of the wounded part.
And let bloodletting be from the opposite side of the wounded part. And let the weak man beware of excess, and wine, and coarse foods.
If anything prohibits diminishment, then he should diminish from food, and not approach flesh, nor wine.
And put on the wound if it happens to him a warm aposteme, a plaster infused in rose oil alone, or with wine in which there is astringency.
If you are safe from the warm aposteme, then put on the wound, if it is recent with its own blood, and the air has not changed it, a powder which I will describe after a little while: and if the air has already changed it, then put on it certain ointments, until it is healed.
If the wound is large, or is from a cut by a sword, and similar things: and its lips do not stick together with threads, then stick them together with a suture, according to what I will describe for wounds of the belly concerning their suture.
If the wound has already been torn from the bone, and is hanging, and there is no retention of it, except in a small suspension, then cut it off. Then treat the wound with medicines, and restore in it hard flesh in place of skin, and order the weak person to be nourished with foods in which there is thickness, such as are heads and cooked wheat, until it is like a pulse: and similar things.
What if you find in the skin putrefaction, and it does not adhere to the bone: then cut off the entire putrid thing, and throw it away: then treat that.
If however in these wounds there is an artery, or a vein from which blood flows: and it is not separated by medicines, then tie above the artery. If therefore you find it not cut, then cut it with a spatula, or tie it. What if necessity demands it when that which we have said does not suffice, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped.
But if these wounds are small and simple, then their treatment is easy and light: so that you powder over them this powder: because it consolidates them before it changes their appearance.
Method of the Powder for Incurring Flesh Wounds. Take one part of olibanum and two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unslaked lime: pound all together much, and sieve: and fill the wound with it, and bind with a good bandage, until it adheres well to the wound, and coagulates with the blood.
Then tie it above with a string, and leave it, and do not loosen it while it remains, so that it does not become an aposteme. For the medicine should not be eradicated from it until it is healed.
And when lime alone does that, when you do not have olibanum and dragon's blood present, and also dragon's blood performs the same operation in many large wounds, when it is suitable to be placed on them and bound, and they are fresh wounds with their own blood, which has not been altered by the air.
For if the wound has already been altered by the air due to some alteration, especially when it is in the summer season, then the intention of this powder is not in position: therefore treat it with what we have said, so that you place on them certain digestive ointments: or place on them poultices made from barley flour, made with water and honey, until they emit pus. Then treat the remaining things with treatment, until they are healed.
If it happens with a wound and a fracture of the bone, and it is small, then extract it with Gestus: and I will already speak about the treatment of fractures of the head in what is to come.
Of the wounds of the neck.
If a wound happens on the neck, then there is no difference between it and a head wound as regards treatment when it is simple.
If the nerve of the neck is cut, or an artery: then if it is a nerve, there is no ingenuity in it, except that the treatment of it must be undertaken with what causes violent constriction, such as ziniar, and zegi, and similar things. For they injure nerves and constrict them.
And you should not put anything cold on the wound at all: for the substance of nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the most elevated of the membranes: and let that with which it is treated be mild medicines, such as calx lota with sweet water infused several times with oil, or with rose oil and tutty, when it is washed also with sweet water: and other mineral stones, in this manner, and moist ointments.
If the wound is large, then administer a suture: or constrict its lips with poultices. Then treat it until it heals.
If the wound has depth, or if a sinus forms on its lower part, in which pus is already collecting, then perforate it in the most depressed place.
For if an artery has been cut in the wound and a flow of its blood follows: then separate, or cut it out, and ligate it: or cauterize it, if necessity calls for that.
If the cartilages of the throat have been cut, or all of them, and the alhaudegi are preserved: then bring together the lips of the skin with a suture over the cane of the throat, and do not touch the throat, but reduce it to its natural figure. Then tighten it with a bandage for some days. Then treat it with ointments which have astringency and excitation, until it is healed.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then perforate it: then if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all of them, or as many as you can: and what is not prepared, leave it, until the wound becomes putrid, and is separated and the protrusion is alleviated.
What if the wound is fresh, then powder over it the powder which I have described. If however a bone is seen in the wound and a fistula is formed: then treat it with that which I have mentioned in its own chapter.
Of the wound on the shoulder blade.
If it is a thrust of a spear or a dagger, and you see its depth, then consider it. If therefore a windiness comes out of the wound, when the weak person breathes from it, then know that the wound is mortal.
What if the depth is not to it, and it is fresh with its blood: then do not put on it powder from the first hour, nor bind it, so that the blood is not retained in its depth, and returns to the heart, and kills the weak person: but put on it an attractive ointment, and dress it twice a day.
If indeed the ointment is not present to you, then put in the opening of the wound old cloth, so that it sucks up what comes out from it due to moistures: and make the weak person sleep on the wound, so that what gathers in it runs.
If indeed the wound has already passed three days, or more, and no spasm has happened to the weak person, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor constriction in breathing, and you see its other dispositions good: then know that the wound is safe. Treatment is applied to it and with bandages, and the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
If the skin is excavated for its healing, and now it always opens, then you should know that a fistula has already been made. Treatment is applied to it from its own chapter.
And if the wound is from a cut of a sword, or a knife, and is simple on the surface of the breast, or back: then treat it with what preceded concerning suture, if it is large: or with powder, if it is small.
If however it has already made an impression on the bone, and a fragment has been cut from it: then investigate the wound, and hasten to extract those fragments, if they are separated. If indeed they are not separated, then leave them alone, until the wound becomes putrid, for the extraction of them will be alleviated.
The judgment of other accidental wounds in other limbs, in treatment, is the same judgment that we have already spoken.
Of wounds of the abdomen, and the protrusion of the intestines, and their treatment.
The disruption that occurs to the abdomen is great, and moderate, and small.
From a great one, therefore, when the intestine, or many of the intestines, protrudes outward.
Which is why their introduction and their suture is more vehement and difficult.
And a small disruption is also made difficult in another way. Therefore it follows that their reduction is more difficult, if you do not hasten to introduce them back to their place immediately: for it swells, opens, and becomes enlarged: which is why the entrance of it becomes difficult.
On account of this therefore, a moderate disruption is better than the others: since with it the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is difficult in these two types.
Know that the suture of a vein is second to four methods.
Two common suture methods come together in the suture of a vein, and in the suture of other wounds of the body; and two other special suture methods are suited to the rest of the wounds. But they are more properly associated with the suture of a vein: and I will describe to you each one with explanation, and declaration.
I say therefore, that when a wound is small, and something comes out of it from the intestine, and it is difficult to reduce it: then it is suitable for one of the two methods. Or because of the smallness of the disruption, as we have said: or since there is inflammation in the intestine on account of cold air.
When therefore it is thus, then it is necessary that you warm it, so that you submerge a sponge, or a moist cloth in warm water alone. Or boil in water cypress and cumin, and spike lavender and chamomile with it on the intestine, until the inflammation is relieved.
Sometimes make a wine in which there is astringency: and it is better than water alone for relieving inflammation.
When therefore you see the inflammation has already been relieved, then moisten the intestine with water in which marshmallow or mallow has been boiled. For by that the entrance of it is alleviated with something small.
But if its return is hastened after this cure, then find in the disruption a little, with an instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut.
And the first cure is better when prepared, than cutting: and there is no need to cut after necessity and lack of an instrument.
Let one part of it be twisted and acute, and the other part not acute, and the extremity subtle not with the subtlety of a spatula, but rather more blunt for a little while: and it is that which resembles a forceps, as you see.
When the wound is enlarged, and the intestine protrudes, then it is necessary that there be a reduction of it according to its natural form in its proper place, if possible, over the wound, because it is better.
When the disruption is large in the lower part of the abdomen, then it is necessary that you make the weak one lie on its back, and put its legs higher than its head. And if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then put its head, and its chest higher than its lower parts.
And similarly if there is a disruption in one of the two parts of the abdomen, then put your intention and your consideration always in this, that the part in which there is a wound be higher than the other part.
And it is necessary that you administer it in large wounds, and in medium wounds.
In small wounds, put it according to what is prepared for you.
Then make that the assistant who holds the disrupted part with their hand is present between your hands, and bring its lips together. Then let him who follows remove from it a suture something after something, and this is the common method of one suture.
And it is that you take a needle, or a number of needles according to the quantity of the wound's depth. Then measure from the edge of the disruption the quantity of a finger ring, that is, of the physician, and fix one needle beyond what you insert in it thread at the two edges of the skin, with the two edges of the suture which is under the skin from the interior, until you make it penetrate from the other side, and you have now brought together two edges of the skin, and two edges of the suture: and there are four rows.
Then tie with double thread around the needle several times from both parts at once, until the two lips of the wound are brought together by a proper union.
Then cut the thickness of the digit and also fix a needle in them: afterwards tie it with a thread, just as you did with the first needle. Do not cease to do that with what you insert from needles until you complete the constriction of the entire wound.
And let the needles be medium between thickness and fineness: for subtle needles easily pierce the flesh: and thick ones are difficult to introduce into the skin: because of that it is necessary that they be medium in fineness and thickness.
And it is not necessary that the needle be fixed in two extreme parts of the skin close together: so that the flesh does not pierce quickly, and the wound opens before its consolidation, and they do not stretch also with the suture, so that the wound is not prevented from consolidation.
Then cut the end of the threads, so that they do not harm the weak part during its sleep: and put pillows made of cloth on all sides, which hold the ends of the threads: and leave them, until you know that the wound is already consolidated.
And this kind of suture with needles is more suitable for small wounds. For one or two needles, or around them, are sufficient for the suture.
The second common suture is that you bring together with the suture four ends: two ends of the skin and two ends of the thread in one place, with a needle in which is a thread wound equal in fineness and thickness.
